# Bug Patterns Index

> **Purpose**: Living knowledge base of bugs encountered during development. Load only the category file you need — loading all patterns at once overflows context.
>
> **Before implementing**: scan the categories and quick-lookup table below. Open the relevant category file for full detail.
> **When you hit a runtime error**: scan the Symptom column below before debugging from scratch.
> **After fixing a new bug**: add an entry to the appropriate category file and update this index.

> **2026-05-27 — BP numbering reconciliation (PLAN-0099 W4 T-W4-03, audit §13.2)**:
> the live high-water mark is currently **BP-592**. Concurrent-plan
> traffic outpaced PLAN-0099's draft-time reservations (PLAN-0089
> Wave K filed BP-588..BP-591; PLAN-0099 W1 T-W1-01 filed BP-592
> before W4 landed). The updated PLAN-0099 reservation map is:
> **BP-595 FILED 2026-05-27** for PLAN-0099 W1 SSE chunk streaming (per the
> audit's original tag — see `docs/audits/2026-05-27-plan-0099-latency-metric-redesign.md` §5).
> Remaining W2 batch row-mix/revenue/AGE reservations shift to
> **BP-593 / BP-594 / BP-596 / BP-601**; **BP-597 / BP-598** for W3 Branch-A fixes
> if they ship. Anyone filing a new BP in the next 72h must (a) scan
> for the current `grep -oE "BP-[0-9]+" docs/BUG_PATTERNS.md | sort -u
> -t- -k2,2n | tail -1` value before picking a number, and (b)
> document the new range here if they reserve a contiguous block.

| BP-361 | Rate-limit TTL window bypass via unconditional `EXPIRE` — `RateLimitMiddleware` calls `await valkey.expire(key, window_seconds)` on every request; Redis `EXPIRE` always resets the TTL, so a sustained flow (1 req/s) never triggers the limit because the window resets each time; fix: only set TTL when the key is new (`if current == 1: await valkey.expire(...)`) | Security & Auth | [bug-patterns/security-auth.md](bug-patterns/security-auth.md#bp-361) |
| BP-362 | Auth guard missing on S9 composition endpoints using `_auth_headers()` factory — routes that use the `_auth_headers(request)` JWT factory (which returns `{}` when unauthenticated) can be accessed without auth; the factory does not enforce auth, it only issues headers; fix: always add explicit `if request.state.user is None: raise HTTPException(401)` before using `_auth_headers()` | Security & Auth | [bug-patterns/security-auth.md](bug-patterns/security-auth.md#bp-362) |

| BP-364 | Test mock not updated after repo refactor from per-item to batch API — when a `get(id)` call per item is refactored to `get_batch(ids)`, tests that mock `entity_repo.get` must also mock `entity_repo.get_batch`; missing mock causes batch result to be empty list even when the test expects populated data; fix: add `entity_repo.get_batch = AsyncMock(return_value=[...])` alongside any existing `entity_repo.get` mock | Testing | [bug-patterns/testing.md](bug-patterns/testing.md#bp-364) |
| BP-365 | `_store_canonical` skip-if-exists serves stale empty canonical to consumers — D-008 guard skips MinIO PUT when the object key already exists; correct for pure retries (same bytes), but breaks when a task is rescheduled after a provider fix: old empty canonical file remains on disk while the outbox records new SHA-256, consumer downloads empty payload and silently drops all rows; fix: always PUT (overwrite) — MinIO PUT is idempotent so retries are safe | Workers & Schedulers | [bug-patterns/worker-scheduler.md](bug-patterns/worker-scheduler.md#bp-365) |
| BP-366 | ISO-3166 alpha-3 codes sent to EODHD `/economic-events` — EODHD economic calendar endpoint requires alpha-2 (US, JP) but seed symbols use alpha-3 (USA, JPN) for cross-dataset consistency; all non-EU symbols returned empty event lists; fix: add `iso3_to_iso2` mapping dict in `_fetch_provider_data` before the API call | Workers & Schedulers | [bug-patterns/worker-scheduler.md](bug-patterns/worker-scheduler.md#bp-366) |

---

## How to Use

1. **Before implementing**: scan the table above for categories matching your task. Open the category file for the relevant BPs.
2. **When you hit a runtime error**: search this table for the error message or symptom.
3. **After fixing a new bug**: append the entry to the appropriate category file, then add a row to the Quick Lookup Table above.

## Adding New Patterns

```
# 1. Open the appropriate category file
# 2. Add a new ## BP-NNN section at the end
# 3. Add a row to the Quick Lookup Table in this index
# 4. Assign the next available BP number
```

> **Legacy note**: The original monolithic BUG_PATTERNS.md (8,775 lines) was restructured into this indexed format on 2026-05-03 to reduce LLM context load. All content is preserved in category files.

| BP-376 | OHLCVChart scroll-to-realtime race condition — when `placeholderData` (initialBars) are provided, the `data?.bars` useEffect fires before async `initChart()` sets `chartRef.current`; the effect calls `scrollToRealTime()` as a no-op but prematurely sets the `hasScrolledToRealTime` guard to `true`; subsequent data arrival with a live chart is blocked by the guard → chart stays scrolled to historical past; fix: add `pendingScrollToRealTime` ref; data effect sets it when `chartRef.current` is null; `initChart` executes deferred scroll after setting `chartRef.current = chart` | Frontend | [bug-patterns/frontend.md](bug-patterns/frontend.md#bp-376) |

| BP-390 | Phase 3 single-session batch rollback loses all prior rows — `provisional_enrichment.py` Phase 3 opens one session for all rows; `session.rollback()` on a failing row rolls back ALL rows 0..N-1 already written in the same session; they stay `status='processing'` until the 30-min stale sweep; fix: `await session.commit()` per-row inside the loop (SummaryWorker pattern) so each row's write is independent | Knowledge Graph | [bug-patterns/knowledge-graph.md](bug-patterns/knowledge-graph.md#bp-390) |
| BP-391 | Port abstract method signature diverges from concrete implementation silently — optional params added to the concrete class but not to the port ABC; mypy checks callers against the port (no error); contract drift is invisible until the param is passed by keyword and hits a `TypeError` at runtime; fix: always update the port abstract method when adding optional params to the concrete implementation | Knowledge Graph | [bug-patterns/knowledge-graph.md](bug-patterns/knowledge-graph.md#bp-391) |
| BP-392 | Noise batch UPDATE is N+1 per-row loop — plan acceptance criterion required a single `WHERE queue_id = ANY(:ids)` batch UPDATE; implementation iterates individual UPDATEs; with batch_limit=50 this is 50 round-trips; fix: `WHERE queue_id = ANY(CAST(:ids AS uuid[]))` with `[str(nid) for nid in all_noise_ids]` | Knowledge Graph | [bug-patterns/knowledge-graph.md](bug-patterns/knowledge-graph.md#bp-392) |
| BP-393 | `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` on partitioned parent table fails on PG16 — PG16 raises "concurrent index creation on partitioned tables is not supported"; only fixed in PG17; Alembic migrations using `autocommit_block()` + `CONCURRENTLY` on a partitioned parent will block all subsequent migrations; fix: use plain `op.create_index()` (non-concurrent) in PG16 — downtime acceptable for dev/thesis, or create CONCURRENTLY on each child partition individually | Intelligence Migrations | [bug-patterns/database-orm.md](bug-patterns/database-orm.md#bp-393) |
| BP-394 | Config field wired in settings + constructor but not passed at instantiation site — feature silently inactive despite config; `summary_worker_force_regen_batch_size` existed in `Settings`, was accepted by `SummaryWorker.__init__`, but `SummaryWorker(sf, llm_client)` in `scheduler.py` never passed the third arg; default `0` used always; pattern: any new optional constructor param needs a corresponding scheduler instantiation line update | Knowledge Graph | [bug-patterns/worker-scheduler.md](bug-patterns/worker-scheduler.md#bp-394) |
| BP-395 | Variable used before assignment in exception handler — `KeyError`/`JSONDecodeError` exception handler references a variable (`raw`) that is only assigned on the success path after the failing line; if the error fires before assignment, the handler raises `NameError` which propagates as an unhandled exception, aborting the entire batch; fix: initialize the variable to a sentinel (`raw: str = ""`) before the try block | NLP Pipeline | [bug-patterns/async-concurrency.md](bug-patterns/async-concurrency.md#bp-395) |
| BP-396 | Security fix partially applied — companion log field left unmasked — when hashing sensitive content in one log field (e.g. `raw_hash`), a parallel field in the SAME log call (e.g. `surface=mention_text[:80]`) goes unmasked; root cause: the fix author focused on the primary sensitive field and missed the companion; pattern: when masking sensitive data in structured logs, scan ALL fields in the same logger call for content derived from user/external input | NLP Pipeline, Knowledge Graph | [bug-patterns/auth-security.md](bug-patterns/auth-security.md#bp-396) |
| BP-398 | External content reaches LLM without length cap or delimiter — `context_snippet` from external article news passed directly to `ExtractionInput.context` without truncation or XML wrapping; adversarial headlines can inject LLM instructions and corrupt entity profiles (indirect prompt injection); fix: `_safe_context = f"<article_context>{context_snippet[:500]}</article_context>"` before `ExtractionInput` construction | Knowledge Graph | [bug-patterns/auth-security.md](bug-patterns/auth-security.md#bp-398) |
| BP-397 | Deterministic ID + partitioned table = false idempotency — `ON CONFLICT` on a partitioned parent must include all partition-key columns AND those columns must be bound deterministically by the caller. Using a stable `event_id` while letting `created_at` default to server-side `now()` defeats the conflict path because every replay produces a different `(event_id, created_at)` tuple and the unique constraint can never match. Concrete example: PLAN-0076 Wave A-3 stabilised `event_id` via `uuid5_from_parts` but missed `created_at`; the QA fix binds `created_at` deterministically (use `event_date` when present, fall back to a stable migration-aligned baseline otherwise) so the full conflict-target tuple is reproducible across replays. | Database & ORM | [bug-patterns/database-orm.md](bug-patterns/database-orm.md#bp-397) |
| BP-399 | Settings env vars not threaded into Kafka consumer call sites — when adding a new env-var-driven config field, all consumer/worker factories that instantiate the relevant class MUST be updated. Concrete example: PLAN-0076 Wave A-4 added `provisional_enrichment_{base,max}_retry_minutes` to `Settings` and threaded them into `ProvisionalEnrichmentWorker.__init__`, but the parallel hot-path consumer factory in `provisional_queued_consumer_main.py` was missed. The hot path silently used the function defaults (2 / 1440) regardless of operator configuration — visible only by inspecting `next_retry_at` values in the DB after a failed batch. Pattern: when adding a config field consumed by a class, grep for every `<ClassName>(` instantiation site and confirm each forwards the new kwarg. | Knowledge Graph, Config | [bug-patterns/worker-scheduler.md](bug-patterns/worker-scheduler.md#bp-399) |
| BP-400 | UNIQUE INDEX migration fails on existing duplicate data — always include a one-time dedup pre-step (merge + repoint FKs + DELETE) BEFORE creating a unique constraint on a populated table; a naked `CREATE UNIQUE INDEX` aborts with `could not create unique index ... because key ... is duplicated` and blocks the entire migration chain. Concrete example: PLAN-0076 Wave A-1 added a UNIQUE INDEX on `canonical_entities(lower(canonical_name))` after the find-then-create dedup race had already left ~132 duplicate rows in production; the QA fix wraps the upgrade in a `DO $$ ... $$` block that selects deterministic keepers (`MIN(created_at)`), repoints every referencing FK table (entity_aliases, entity_embedding_state, relations, relation_evidence_raw, claims, events, event_entities, entity_event_exposures, provisional_entity_queue, relation_summaries), DELETEs the doomed rows, and only then creates the partial unique index. Pattern: BEFORE adding a unique constraint to a populated column, run the equivalent dedup query in a staging DB to discover the actual duplicate count, and bake the merge logic into the same migration so the upgrade is atomic. | Intelligence Migrations | [bug-patterns/database-orm.md](bug-patterns/database-orm.md#bp-400) |
| BP-401 | Postgres tsvector GENERATED columns must read from in-row text content, not from external-storage object keys. PLAN-0063 W5-2 originally generated `chunks.tsv_english` from `coalesce(chunk_text_key, '')`, but `chunk_text_key` holds a MinIO object path (`nlp-pipeline/chunk-text/<uuid>/<uuid>/body/v1.txt`), not the body — so the index tokenized UUIDs and `body/v1.txt` instead of analyst terms. **Symptoms**: green integration tests (the test fixture seeded body text into the wrong column to make assertions match) + zero matches against production data despite thousands of populated rows. **Fix**: add a denormalised `chunk_text TEXT` column populated from the in-memory body at insert time; point GENERATED tsvectors at the body column. **Detection rule**: any GENERATED tsvector that references a `*_key` / `*_uri` / `*_path` column is suspect — verify the column actually holds searchable content by sampling a row in psql. **Test rule**: integration test fixtures must populate the SAME columns the production writer populates; never stuff body content into a key/path column to make FTS match. | Database & ORM, NLP Pipeline | [bug-patterns/database-orm.md](bug-patterns/database-orm.md#bp-401) |
| BP-402 | `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` silently preserves a column with stale GENERATED expression — when a previous test bootstrap created `tsv_english` with the old expression, the same `IF NOT EXISTS` line in the next test session is a no-op, so the test DB drifts from the migration even after source files are updated. **Symptom**: integration tests fail with 0 matches even though the migration looks correct on disk; manual `\d chunks` shows the GENERATED expression still references the old source column. **Fix in test bootstrap**: drop the GENERATED columns + their indexes BEFORE re-creating, so each test session starts from clean DDL (the production migration is fine — it runs once per upgrade; the trap is specific to long-lived test DBs). **Detection rule**: any test fixture that bootstraps GENERATED columns via `IF NOT EXISTS` on a session-scoped DB is at risk. | NLP Pipeline, Test Fixtures | [bug-patterns/database-orm.md](bug-patterns/database-orm.md#bp-402) |
| BP-403 | SQLAlchemy `AsyncSession` is NOT safe for concurrent use — running two `asyncio.create_task` legs that both call into the same session via `asyncio.gather` raises `IllegalStateChangeError: Method 'close()' can't be called here; method '_connection_for_bind()' is already in progress`. PLAN-0063 W5-3 hit this when the hybrid use-case fanned ANN + lexical legs through `self._repo` (one session). **Symptom**: every hybrid request returns HTTP 500 with the IllegalStateChangeError stack; tests using a mocked repo never see it because mocks don't enforce the contract. **Fixes (in order of preference)**: (1) inject a session-factory and have each concurrent leg open its own session — true parallelism, max+something latency; (2) serialize the legs (`await leg1; await leg2`) — correctness over latency, ~max+min latency, what PLAN-0063 W5-3 shipped as the immediate fix; (3) move concurrency outside the session boundary (e.g. background prefetch). **Detection rule**: any `asyncio.gather` / `asyncio.wait` / `asyncio.as_completed` over coroutines that touch a shared `AsyncSession` is suspect — verify each branch uses a distinct session OR runs sequentially. | NLP Pipeline, Async & Concurrency | [bug-patterns/async-concurrency.md](bug-patterns/async-concurrency.md#bp-403) |
| BP-407 | Multi-step Redis sorted-set sequences (ZADD → ZREMRANGEBYSCORE → ZCARD → EXPIRE) are NOT atomic when issued via `pipeline(transaction=False)` — commands are batched but may interleave with concurrent writers, so two coroutines can both observe `count < threshold` and one circuit-breaker trip is missed even though both writers committed their ZADD. **Fix**: wrap the entire sequence in a Lua script invoked via `EVAL` — Redis guarantees Lua scripts run atomically and isolated on the server. **Detection rule**: any read-after-write pipeline whose decision depends on the read result is suspect; if the decision is "did we cross a threshold", convert to Lua. Concrete example: PLAN-0076 Wave B-2 / DEF-031 — `SourceCircuitBreaker.record_failure()` was changed from a 4-step pipeline to a single `_RECORD_FAILURE_LUA` script via the new `ValkeyClient.execute_lua_script()` helper. **Renumbered from BP-403 on 2026-05-07** (QA-PLAN-0063 collision; the SQLAlchemy AsyncSession concurrent-use pattern at BP-403 was assigned first by PLAN-0063 W5-3). | rag-chat, libs/messaging | [bug-patterns/distributed.md](bug-patterns/distributed.md#bp-407) |
| BP-404 | `prometheus_client` Counter/Histogram `MetricFamily.name` strips the `_total` suffix in newer versions (≥0.16) — `MetricFamily.name` for a Counter named `foo_total` is `"foo"`, but individual `Sample.name` values retain `"foo_total"`. Tests that check `m.name == "foo_total"` always get zero even after calling `.inc()`. **Fix**: query `s.name` (Sample-level) rather than `m.name` (MetricFamily-level) when filtering for a specific counter in `REGISTRY.collect()`: `for m in REGISTRY.collect(): for s in m.samples: if s.name == "foo_total" ...`. **Additional pitfall**: Counter values accumulate across the entire test session (Prometheus REGISTRY is a process-wide singleton). Use unique label values per test (e.g. `source="unit_test_w55"`) to avoid `before + 1` assertions being contaminated by increments from other tests in the same session. | Testing | [bug-patterns/testing.md](bug-patterns/testing.md#bp-404) |
| BP-405 | Implementation plan references a class/method/port-field that does not exist (stale assumption). Three concurrent plans (PLAN-0066/0067/0074) referenced `ChatOrchestratorUseCase` / `RunChatUseCase` and `ChunkSearchRequest.entity_tickers` / `entity_mentions` — none existed. Names *read correctly* so human review didn't catch it. **Fix is mechanical, not editorial**: (a) `/plan` and `/revise-prd` skills add a `git grep` verification step for every named class/method/port/file before plan freeze; (b) `/implement` halts on first wave if a non-tagged target is missing; (c) untagged names default to "must already exist" — new shapes must be tagged `(NEW — created in this plan)`. | API & Contracts | [bug-patterns/api-contracts.md](bug-patterns/api-contracts.md#bp-405) |
| BP-406 | Singleton DI of a per-request collaborator silently strips auth/scope context. PLAN-0067 W11-2's `ToolExecutor.__init__(... user_id=None, tenant_id=None, x_internal_token=None)` would either (a) be wired as singleton and carry `None` forever (silent portfolio-tool disabling, possible cross-tenant data leak under future tools), or (b) be wired per-request and waste collaborator resolution. **Fix**: split into `<Class>Factory` (singleton, holds shared collaborators) + `<Class>` (per-request, holds auth/scope). Factory exposes `for_request(*, user_id, tenant_id, jwt, entity_context) -> Class`. Per-LLM-call signatures stay clean. **Rule R30**: per-request auth context never goes into singleton `__init__`. | API & Contracts | [bug-patterns/api-contracts.md](bug-patterns/api-contracts.md#bp-406) |
| BP-408 | Fix-Induced Test Regressions from Touched-File-Only Testing — fix applied to one file, only that file's tests run, regressions in other importing files go undetected. Common sources: AsyncMock/MagicMock confusion, side_effect list length mismatches, UUID/string validation changes breaking 'UNKNOWN' string tests. Prevention: always run the full service test suite after any fix. | Testing | [bug-patterns/testing.md](bug-patterns/testing.md#bp-408) |
| BP-409 | Subagent Worktree Commit Loss — parallel fix agents apply changes in isolated worktrees but do not commit before returning; changes silently discarded when worktree is cleaned up; orchestrating agent sees "success" but the fix is absent from main. Prevention: every subagent must `git commit` before returning; orchestrator must verify commits landed. | Testing | [bug-patterns/testing.md](bug-patterns/testing.md#bp-409) |
| BP-410 | Container/Source Divergence: Fix Applied to Source But Running Container Has Old Code — source edited and unit tests pass but Docker image never rebuilt; live endpoint still shows the bug; `docker compose restart` keeps the old image. Fix: `docker compose build <svc> && docker compose up -d --no-deps <svc>` after every runtime fix commit. Related: BP-257, BP-319, BP-346. | Config & Docker | [bug-patterns/config-docker.md](bug-patterns/config-docker.md#bp-410) |
| BP-411 | ID Namespace Collision When Assigning R-Numbers, BP-Numbers, or PLAN-Numbers — new number assigned from memory without grepping the canonical file; collision creates two entries with the same ID making all references ambiguous. Prevention: `grep -o 'BP-[0-9]\+' docs/BUG_PATTERNS.md \| sort -t- -k2 -n \| tail -5` before assigning any new number. | API & Contracts | [bug-patterns/api-contracts.md](bug-patterns/api-contracts.md#bp-411) |
| BP-412 | Use case implemented + tested in isolation but never wired in `app.py` lifespan — a use case has passing unit tests but no caller in `app.py` lifespan (no `asyncio.create_task`, no `_wire_*`, no `await uc.execute()` in startup). The behaviour (Prometheus gauge update, cron job, metric increment) is silently dead: the gauge stays at 0 forever, the cron never fires, the metric never increments. Symptom: unit tests all green; live metric never changes; feature appears to work when called directly but is never triggered. Detection: grep `lifespan` in `app.py`; compare to the full use-case/worker list in the service. Fix: wire in lifespan behind an opt-in env-flag (`<FEATURE>_ENABLED`) with a done-callback BP-268 pattern. Reference: F-A01 (PLAN-0084 A-1). | Architecture | [bug-patterns/api-contracts.md](bug-patterns/api-contracts.md#bp-412) |
| BP-413 | Circuit breaker with no HALF_OPEN probe gating; cooldown expiry → stampede on the recovering source — `is_open()` returns `state == "open"` without a SETNX probe slot. When the cooldown expires ALL in-flight callers are admitted simultaneously, hammering the recovering source and likely retriggering the circuit before the first probe response returns. Detection: any breaker `is_open()` implementation that just compares `state` without a SETNX/atomic probe key is suspect. Fix: add a SETNX probe key with a short TTL (`probe_ttl_seconds=5`); only the first caller per TTL window is admitted in `HALF_OPEN` state; all others still short-circuit until the probe succeeds. Reference: F-X01 (PLAN-0084 A-2). | Architecture | [bug-patterns/distributed.md](bug-patterns/distributed.md#bp-413) |
| BP-414 | Cache populated once at startup, never refreshed (DS-009 stale-replica pattern) — a cache class has a `refresh()` method called once at startup inside `lifespan`. After the first population the cache is never updated. Any source changes (new canonicals, updated entity definitions, Valkey key expiry) are invisible until the service restarts. Detection: grep for `refresh()` callsites; if the only callsite is at startup with no background loop, the cache is suspect. Fix: add `_refresh_loop()` async task launched via `asyncio.create_task(self._refresh_loop())` in `start()`; cancel the task in `close()` using a `done_callback` or `task.cancel()`. Reference: F-X02 (PLAN-0084 C-1). | Architecture | [bug-patterns/api-contracts.md](bug-patterns/api-contracts.md#bp-414) |
| BP-415 | Hand-rolled `is_duplicate` / `mark_processed` per consumer drifts into multiple dialects — each `BaseKafkaConsumer` subclass implementing its own dedup logic leads to divergent TTL policies, missing at-least-once fallback on Valkey errors, inconsistent key-naming taxonomies, and hard-to-test dedup behaviour. Common manifestations: `return False` stubs that silently disable dedup; per-consumer Valkey calls with non-canonical key formats; TTLs that don't match the message replay window. Detection: architecture test `test_consumer_dedup_mixin_enforcement` (CONSUMER-DEDUP-001) flags non-compliant consumers. Fix: inherit `ValkeyDedupMixin` from `libs/messaging.kafka.consumer.dedup`; set `_dedup_prefix` (unique per consumer, e.g. `content_ingestion:dedup:article_raw`) and optionally `_dedup_ttl_seconds` (default 86 400); add justified exceptions to `tests/architecture/_consumer_dedup_allowlist.yaml`. Reference: F-X11/F-X12/F-D03 (PLAN-0084 B-1..B-3). | Architecture | [bug-patterns/distributed.md](bug-patterns/distributed.md#bp-415) |
| BP-416 | Unbounded `float` pydantic-settings field silently accepts `NaN` and negative values — a bare `float` field with no `Field(ge=...)` constraint passes pydantic validation with `NaN`, `-5.0`, or `inf` inputs. At runtime `min(1.0, max(0.0, nan))` collapses to `0.0` for EVERY item in the response (total silent ranking failure) with no startup error and no log warning. Pattern: `RAG_CHAT_TRUST_W_SOURCE=nan` causes all fusion scores to zero out while the service appears healthy. Fix: add `Field(default=<n>, ge=0.0, le=<max>)` to every numeric settings field that feeds a formula. Detection: grep for `float = ` (bare float field) in Settings classes; any without `Field(ge=...)` is suspect when used in arithmetic. Note: `ge=` also rejects `NaN` because pydantic's `ge` validator calls `value >= 0.0` which is `False` for NaN. See: `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/config.py` — fixed in PLAN-0079 QA sprint. | Config & Docker | [bug-patterns/config-docker.md](bug-patterns/config-docker.md#bp-416) |
| BP-417 | Nested DB session inside already-open session creates two independent transactions — partial write on commit failure. A method called within an open `async with session_factory() as session` block that itself opens `async with self._session_factory() as session2` creates a second, independent transaction. If the outer commit succeeds and the inner commit fails (or vice versa), the data is partially written with no automatic rollback. Symptom: service appears healthy, first half of data is persisted, second half is silently lost. Detection: grep for `async with.*session_factory` inside methods that are called within an already-open session context. Fix: pass the active session as a parameter rather than opening a new one. Reference: D-013 (PLAN-0084 QA). | Kafka & Messaging | [bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md](bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md#bp-417) |
| BP-418 | Fire-and-forget Kafka produce after DB commit creates a permanent loss window for one-time lifecycle events — a direct `producer.produce()` call placed AFTER `session.commit()` (outside any transaction) creates a window where a process crash or network error drops the event permanently. For frequently-repeated events (e.g. entity embeddings refreshed on every article) this is acceptable since the next occurrence re-triggers. For one-time lifecycle events (entity promoted from provisional, entity deleted, relationship first-established) the loss is permanent: the entity/relation never reaches the downstream pipeline. Symptom: DB shows the entity promoted, but downstream service (embeddings, enrichment) never receives the trigger. Detection: any `producer.produce()` call after a `session.commit()` without an outbox intermediary is suspect for one-time lifecycle events. Fix: use outbox pattern (`outbox_repo.add()` + dispatcher) for lifecycle events; fire-and-forget acceptable only for high-frequency repeat events. Reference: D-014 (PLAN-0084 QA). | Kafka & Messaging | [bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md](bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md#bp-418) |
| BP-419 | Dual-session consumer with silent second-session commit swallow + early-skip = permanent data loss on failure — a consumer that opens two sessions (nlp_session + intel_session) and swallows the second commit failure on the grounds that "the write is idempotent on retry" fails to account for an early-exit guard (e.g. "skip if routing_decision already exists") that fires on re-delivery. The first session commits; the second fails silently; on Kafka re-delivery the early-skip fires; the second session's writes are permanently skipped. The "idempotent on retry" claim is technically true for the WRITE but the retry never happens. Symptom: entity mentions extracted by the NLP pipeline never appear in the KG, despite routing_decisions showing the article was processed. Detection: any `except Exception: logger.warning(...) # DON'T re-raise` after a second-session commit in a dual-session consumer is a red flag. Fix: re-raise the second-session exception (nack the message); add Prometheus counter for second-session failures; add a guard that re-runs second-session writes even when the first-session early-skip fires. Reference: D-010 (PLAN-0084 QA). | Kafka & Messaging | [bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md](bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md#bp-419) |
| BP-421 | Hand-rolled `is_duplicate` / `mark_processed` in a `BaseKafkaConsumer` subclass without try/except on Valkey calls crashes the consumer on any Valkey outage. When `self._dedup_client.exists()` or `.set()` raises (ConnectionError, TimeoutError), the exception propagates through `_handle_message()` into `_handle_failure()` — the consumer stalls or enters retry hell for the duration of the outage. If `mark_processed()` fails after the DB commit has already succeeded, the consumer treats a successful message as a failure, producing a duplicate on re-delivery. Fix: use `ValkeyDedupMixin` from `libs/messaging.kafka.consumer.dedup`, which wraps Valkey calls in try/except with fail-open semantics (returns False on check failure, swallows mark failure). Detection: architecture test `CONSUMER-DEDUP-001`. Reference: C-1 (PLAN-0084 QA Wave 6). | Kafka & Messaging | [bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md](bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md#bp-421) |
| BP-422 | Redis MULTI/EXEC cache swap (DEL + SADD same key) wipes the cache on network drop — MULTI/EXEC is atomic on the server once EXEC is processed, but if the client loses connectivity after the server queues DEL, the key is deleted and SADD never runs. `pipe.execute()` raises; the except block logs a warning; the cache is empty until the next successful refresh. Fix: replace MULTI/EXEC with a Lua script invoked via `EVAL` — Lua scripts are atomic on the server with no partial-failure window. Pattern: any `pipeline(transaction=True)` block that issues `pipe.delete(key)` followed by `pipe.sadd(key, ...)` is suspect. Related: BP-407 (Redis multi-step atomicity for counters). Reference: C-2 (PLAN-0084 QA Wave 6). | Architecture, NLP Pipeline | [bug-patterns/distributed.md](bug-patterns/distributed.md#bp-422) |
| BP-423 | Fixed retry interval in background `while True` loop causes log spam and operator blindness during sustained outages — `await asyncio.sleep(FIXED_N)` on every exception emits O(duration/N) identical warning tracebacks with no indication of how long the loop has been failing. Fix: exponential backoff with a ceiling (e.g. `min(2**failures * 60, 300)`) + a Prometheus counter for consecutive failures so alerting can fire on `consecutive_failures > 5`. Detection: any `except Exception: await asyncio.sleep(CONSTANT)` inside a `while True` loop in a `_*_loop` or `_run_*` method is a candidate. Reference: C-3 (PLAN-0084 QA Wave 6). | Architecture, Observability | [bug-patterns/distributed.md](bug-patterns/distributed.md#bp-423) |
| BP-424 | Disabled-feature test guard prevents the code under test from running — a test patches a function, then wraps the call to `_wire_<feature>` or the equivalent function in `if settings.<flag>:`. With the flag disabled the function is never called; `mock.assert_not_called()` trivially passes. The test provides zero coverage of the flag-evaluation logic in the actual wiring code. Fix: call the function under test unconditionally inside the test — let the function decide its own behaviour based on settings. Detection: `mock_x.assert_not_called()` in a test that also has `if settings.X:` guarding the function call that would invoke `mock_x`. Reference: QA-003 (PLAN-0084 QA Wave 6). | Testing | [bug-patterns/testing.md](bug-patterns/testing.md#bp-424) |
| BP-425 | Prometheus `REGISTRY` global state leaks between unit tests — `prometheus_client.REGISTRY` is a process-wide singleton; tests that register metric labels accumulate state across the session and race in parallel runs (pytest -n). Unique label values per test (BP-404 workaround) reduce noise but do not eliminate races. Fix: provide an `isolated_registry` fixture in `conftest.py` that monkeypatches `prometheus_client.REGISTRY` to a fresh `CollectorRegistry` per test. All metric-assertion tests should accept `isolated_registry` as a fixture and read from it instead of the global `REGISTRY`. Related: BP-404. Reference: QA-008 (PLAN-0084 QA Wave 6). | Testing | [bug-patterns/testing.md](bug-patterns/testing.md#bp-425) |
| BP-420 | Phone-number regex false positive on SEC CIK numbers and other bare 10-digit identifiers — `\b(\+?1[-.\s]?)?\(?\d{3}\)?[-.\s]?\d{3}[-.\s]?\d{4}\b` matches "0000320193" (Apple CIK) as a phone number because all separators are optional. Symptom: `PIIDetectedError` on eval queries containing financial identifiers; eval harness returns HTTP 500 on `POST /v1/internal/retrieve` for queries like "CIK 0000320193 filings". Fix: make separators mandatory — remove all `?` from the separator groups: `\b(\+?1[-.\s])?\(?\d{3}\)?[-.\s]\d{3}[-.\s]\d{4}\b`. This still matches `(800) 555-1234`, `800-555-1234`, `800.555.1234` but correctly rejects bare 10-digit runs like CIK codes. Also apply the same fix to `_SSN_RE`: require dashes/spaces between groups. Detection: any `_PHONE_RE.search("0000320193")` returns a match — run `python3 -c "import re; print(re.compile(r'<pattern>').search('0000320193'))"` against any PII pattern that has optional separators. Reference: PLAN-0084 E-3. | rag-chat | [bug-patterns/api-contracts.md](bug-patterns/api-contracts.md#bp-420) |
| BP-426 | Valkey ZADD timestamp-as-member coalesces sub-second failures — when `time.time()` is used as both the ZADD score AND member, consecutive failures within the same clock tick share the same float value. Because ZADD members must be unique within a ZSET, the second ZADD overwrites the first entry instead of adding a new entry; ZCARD returns a lower count than the real failure rate. On macOS, measured 957/999 consecutive `time.time()` calls returning identical floats (95.7%). Fix: append a short unique suffix to the ZADD member to guarantee uniqueness while keeping the score as the real timestamp for ZRANGEBYSCORE pruning: `member = f"{timestamp}:{new_uuid7().hex[:8]}"` (use `common.ids.new_uuid7()` — never `uuid.uuid4()` per R10/IG-COMMON-001; the time-prefix component of the UUIDv7 is irrelevant since only the hex tail is used for uniqueness). Detection: any `redis.call('ZADD', key, now, now)` in a Lua script or `zadd(key, {now: now})` in Python code is suspect when the caller is a circuit breaker or rate limiter that relies on ZCARD for threshold decisions. Reference: F-DS005 (PLAN-0084 QA Wave 7 deferred); fix landed via QA-PLAN-0083 /fix-bug 2026-05-08. | rag-chat | [bug-patterns/distributed.md](bug-patterns/distributed.md#bp-426) |
| BP-427 | rag-chat Alembic migration must use raw `op.execute("ALTER TABLE …")` SQL strings, not the `op.add_column()` Python API, for column additions to tables covered by `tests/unit/infrastructure/test_ddl_alignment.py`. The DDL alignment test parses migration files with a regex over `CREATE TABLE` and `ALTER TABLE … ADD COLUMN [IF NOT EXISTS]` SQL strings — `op.add_column()` calls are invisible to the regex. New columns added with the Python API will pass migrations at runtime but make the alignment guard fail with `ORM columns missing from DDL: {'<col>'}`. Convention is established by migration `0002_add_context_valkey_keys.py` (raw SQL). Fix: write migrations as `op.execute("ALTER TABLE <table> ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS <col> <type> [REFERENCES …] [ON DELETE …]")`. Detection: grep for `op.add_column` in `services/rag-chat/alembic/versions/`. Long-term: extending the alignment regex to also recognise `op.add_column()` calls would remove the convention requirement, but the convention is simpler to enforce at authoring time. Reference: /investigate 2026-05-08 (PLAN-0066 Wave D regression). | rag-chat | [bug-patterns/database.md](bug-patterns/database.md#bp-427) |
| BP-428 | `from fastapi import …, Field, …` is invalid — `Field` is a `pydantic` symbol, not a `fastapi` symbol. Symptom: `ImportError: cannot import name 'Field' from 'fastapi'` on module load (and therefore on container startup, since FastAPI route modules are imported at app boot). Authors who intend to use `Field(ge=0, …)` for Pydantic validation in request/response models often add the import to the existing fastapi line by reflex. Correct location: `from pydantic import BaseModel, Field`. Detection: a one-line ripgrep guard pre-commit — `rg "from fastapi import.*\\bField\\b" services/ libs/` should match nothing. Long-term: a pre-commit hook for this exact pattern would prevent the regression entirely; the bug is high-impact (full service unbootable) and the detection is trivial. Reference: /investigate 2026-05-08 (PLAN-0066 Wave C regression — rag-chat unbootable until import fixed). | All FastAPI services | [bug-patterns/imports.md](bug-patterns/imports.md#bp-428) |
| BP-429 | `ToolExecutorFactory` not wired in `app.py` lifespan — when a new factory/service is added in a use-case constructor but `app.py`'s lifespan/`_wire_orchestrator` function is not updated, the factory defaults to `None` and the use-case falls back to the old code path or raises `AttributeError` at first request. The service starts, tests pass (tests inject the factory directly), but production traffic gets broken behaviour. Detection: after adding any new required dependency to a use-case `__init__`, grep for every instantiation site of that use case (including `app.py`). | BP-430 | `ToolUseBlock.id` vs `.tool_use_id` attribute mismatch between LLM response parsing and downstream consumers — `ToolUseBlock` (in `libs/tools/src/tools/types.py`) exposes `.id` as its canonical field name (matching OpenAI tool-call format). Handlers that reference `.tool_use_id` (the Anthropic API field name) get `AttributeError`. Symptom: `ToolCallProvenance` silently records an empty `call_id`, breaking citation audit trails. Fix: use `getattr(tool_call, 'id', None) or getattr(tool_call, 'tool_use_id', '')` at handler callsites during migration; long-term, standardise on `.id` everywhere. | BP-431 | `.dockerignore` allowlist omits a new shared library — when `libs/tools/` (or any new shared lib) is added to a service Dockerfile via `COPY libs/tools/src ...`, the root `.dockerignore` (which uses `*` deny-all + `!` allowlist strategy) must also add `!libs/tools/pyproject.toml` and `!libs/tools/src/` entries. Without these, Docker build fails with `failed to compute cache key: "/libs/tools/src": not found` even though the directory exists on disk. Detection: after adding a new COPY for a library in any Dockerfile, verify the root `.dockerignore` has a corresponding `!` entry. | BP-432 | Partial-granularity ANN search missing tenant filter — when an ANN search method supports multiple granularities (chunk/section/both), each leg has its own SQL method. Adding a tenant filter to ONE leg (e.g. `_search_chunks`) without updating ALL legs (e.g. `_search_sections`) leaves a silent data-isolation gap. The chunk path is secure; `granularity="section"` or `"both"` returns every tenant's private sections. Symptom: chunk-level RAG appears secure; section-level or mixed queries leak cross-tenant document content. Detection: for every `_search_*` method in a repository, verify `tenant_id` is both in the method signature AND in the WHERE clause. HR-053 invariant: `tenant_id=None` → `IS NULL` (public only), NOT no filter. The no-filter case is always wrong when private content exists. Fix: add the same `(tenant_id IS NULL OR tenant_id = CAST(:t AS UUID)) / IS NULL` predicate to every search leg. Also scope the companion count query — a global `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM section_embeddings` leaks the total volume of all tenants' data. Reference: PLAN-0086 QA CRIT-1 / HR-053. | nlp-pipeline, Architecture | [bug-patterns/security.md](bug-patterns/security.md#bp-432) |
| BP-433 | Pipeline trigger TODO never implemented — use case leaves a `# TODO Wave E-2: append outbox event here` comment that is never followed up. The document status is stuck at PROCESSING forever because no downstream service ever receives a trigger event. Unit tests pass (they mock the outbox), CI is green, but end-to-end flow is broken: uploaded files never progress past PROCESSING. Detection: grep for `# TODO` inside `async with self._uow:` blocks in use cases that manage entity lifecycle; any TODO for an outbox event publish is a blocking gap. Prevention: add a test that asserts `outbox.append.assert_awaited_once()` in the happy-path test; a missing call fails immediately. Reference: PLAN-0086 QA pipeline trigger gap. | content-ingestion | [bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md](bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md#bp-433) |
| BP-434 | Non-deterministic `new_uuid7()` used as outbox `event_id` for idempotency-sensitive events — when an outbox event represents a one-time lifecycle transition (delete, promote, archive), the event_id MUST be deterministic so the outbox `ON CONFLICT (event_id) DO NOTHING` guard deduplicates retries. Using `new_uuid7()` generates a fresh ID on every retry, producing a new outbox row each time; the downstream consumer receives duplicate events. For truly idempotent writes (DELETEs without side effects) this is harmless; for events that trigger external state changes (Kafka fan-out, MinIO GC, KG updates) duplicates cause double-processing. Pattern: `uuid5_from_parts(str(aggregate_id), "event_type_stable_suffix")` gives a stable UUID5 for the same (entity, event-type) pair. Any `new_uuid7()` used as `event_id` in a delete/transition outbox append is suspect. Reference: PLAN-0086 QA MAJ-3. | content-ingestion, Architecture | [bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md](bug-patterns/kafka-messaging.md#bp-434) |
| BP-435 | Architecture enforcement test cited in plan as existing but never created — rule silently unenforced. A plan bullet says "the architecture test `tests/architecture/test_X.py` will fail if Y is not done" as a safety mechanism, but the test was never actually created. The rule (e.g. R29 manifest sync) appears enforced on paper but has zero runtime enforcement; violations introduced by future waves are never caught. Symptom: zero failing tests even when the invariant is violated; `revise-prd` audit catches the gap. Detection (mechanical): for every architecture-test reference in a plan, `ls` the path — if it returns "no such file", the enforcement is phantom. Fix: the wave that introduces the enforcement claim must also create the test in the same commit; the test must be listed explicitly in the wave's scope table. Reference: PLAN-0080 revise-prd 2026-05-09 (R29 `test_tool_manifest_sync.py`). | Testing | [bug-patterns/testing.md](bug-patterns/testing.md#bp-435) |
| BP-436 | `new_uuid7()` referenced as Postgres column DEFAULT before the function was created — migrations 0031, 0032, and 0036 in `intelligence-migrations` used `DEFAULT new_uuid7()` in `CREATE TABLE` DDL, but the function was never registered in Postgres. Earlier migrations used the built-in `gen_random_uuid()` so the gap was invisible. Symptom: `intelligence-migrations` exits non-zero at revision 0031 with `psycopg2.errors.UndefinedFunction: function new_uuid7() does not exist`; the migration chain stalls at revision 0029; all services that depend on tables created in 0032+ (e.g., `path_insight_jobs`, `entity_narrative_versions`) crash-loop with `UndefinedTableError`. Fix: add `CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION new_uuid7() RETURNS UUID LANGUAGE plpgsql` at the top of migration 0031's `upgrade()`. The function generates a standards-compliant UUIDv7 (RFC 9562): 48-bit millisecond timestamp, 4-bit version (0x7), 12-bit rand_a, 2-bit variant (0b10), 62-bit rand_b. Detection: any Alembic migration using `DEFAULT new_uuid7()` in DDL; `SELECT prosrc FROM pg_proc WHERE proname = 'new_uuid7'` returning 0 rows. Reference: path-insight-worker crash investigation 2026-05-09. | intelligence-migrations | [bug-patterns/database.md](bug-patterns/database.md#bp-436) |
| BP-437 | `CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY` used on a Postgres *partitioned* table — Postgres does not support `CONCURRENTLY` index creation on partition parents (relkind='p'). The command must be run on each partition individually or non-concurrently on the parent. Symptom: `psycopg2.errors.FeatureNotSupported: cannot create index on partitioned table "relations" concurrently` in migration 0033. Fix: remove `CONCURRENTLY` and the `autocommit_block()` wrapper; replace with plain `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS` — the non-concurrent form runs inside the migration transaction and propagates the index to all existing and future partitions automatically. Detection: `grep -r "CONCURRENTLY" services/intelligence-migrations/alembic/versions/` — cross-check each table against `SELECT relkind FROM pg_class WHERE relname = '<table>'`: relkind='p' means partitioned, cannot use CONCURRENTLY. Reference: migration 0033 failure 2026-05-09. | intelligence-migrations | [bug-patterns/database.md](bug-patterns/database.md#bp-437) |
| BP-438 | Cross-database backfill in Alembic migration references a table that does not exist in the target schema — migration 0035 used `UPDATE … FROM document_source_metadata` where `document_source_metadata` lives in `content_store_db` (S5), not in `intelligence_db`. Even though the migration comment said "this will be a no-op in standalone intelligence_db", Postgres raises `UndefinedTable` before returning zero rows. Symptom: `psycopg2.errors.UndefinedTable: relation "document_source_metadata" does not exist`. Fix: wrap the cross-DB backfill in a `DO $$ BEGIN … EXCEPTION WHEN undefined_table THEN RAISE NOTICE '…'; END; $$` anonymous block so the migration succeeds gracefully when the table is absent. Detection: any Alembic `UPDATE … FROM <table>` that joins to a table potentially absent from the target DB; check with `SELECT tablename FROM pg_tables WHERE tablename = '<table>'` before relying on a join. Reference: migration 0035 failure 2026-05-09. | intelligence-migrations | [bug-patterns/database.md](bug-patterns/database.md#bp-438) |
| BP-439 | `sa.text()` `:param::type` cast notation causes psycopg2 SyntaxError when mixed with `%(key)s` parameters — SQLAlchemy uses psycopg2's `%(param)s` parameter style at the driver level. Inside `sa.text()`, `:param` bindparams work for regular types, but `:param::jsonb` (using the Postgres double-colon cast) triggers a SyntaxError because psycopg2 misparses `::` after a bindparam placeholder. Symptom: `psycopg2.errors.SyntaxError: syntax error at or near ":"` in migration 0036 seed INSERT. Fix (two options): (1) replace `:param::type` with `CAST(:param AS type)` or (2) inline compile-time constants as f-string SQL with `CAST('...' AS jsonb)` to avoid parameterisation entirely. For migration seed data (constant values known at authoring time), option 2 is simpler and safe (no user input). Detection: grep for `::\w` in `sa.text()` strings anywhere in migration files or repository classes. Reference: migration 0036 failure 2026-05-09. | intelligence-migrations | [bug-patterns/database.md](bug-patterns/database.md#bp-439) |
| BP-440 | Postgres tsvector search must use parameterised `websearch_to_tsquery`, not `to_tsquery` with string concatenation — using `to_tsquery(f"..." + user_input)` for full-text search exposes an injection vector because special tsquery operators (`&`, `|`, `!`, `<->`) in user input can alter the query tree. Fix: always use `websearch_to_tsquery('english', :q)` with a bound parameter. `websearch_to_tsquery` auto-escapes all tsquery operators and supports user-facing phrase syntax (`"exact phrase"`, `OR`, `-`). Never use `to_tsquery` with string concatenation. Detection: grep for `to_tsquery` in any repository file — if the call uses f-string or `+` concatenation rather than a bound `:param`, it is vulnerable. Status: CLOSED (guarded at design time; AD-W6-3 in PLAN-0064). Reference: `services/nlp-pipeline/src/nlp_pipeline/infrastructure/nlp_db/repositories/document_search.py`. | Database & ORM, Auth & Security | [bug-patterns/database-orm.md](bug-patterns/database-orm.md#bp-440) |
| BP-441 | Cross-DB joins must be replaced by use-case HTTP batch calls (R9) — when a search repository in service S6 needs entity names from `canonical_entities` (which lives in `intelligence_db`, owned by S7), the initial design may assume a SQL JOIN is possible. This is an R9 violation: the two databases have separate connection pools and are owned by different services. Symptom: `UndefinedTable: relation "canonical_entities" does not exist` when the repository runs in the nlp-pipeline context. Fix: the use case fetches entity names via `POST /api/v1/entities/batch` (S7 HTTP) in parallel with `POST /api/v1/documents/batch` (S5 HTTP) using `asyncio.gather`. The SQL query returns only IDs; enrichment is the use case's responsibility. Pattern: any `JOIN` from a table in `nlp_db` to a table in `intelligence_db` (or any cross-service DB join) is an R9 violation. Status: CLOSED (architectural decision AD-W6-3 in PLAN-0064). Reference: `services/nlp-pipeline/src/nlp_pipeline/application/use_cases/search_documents.py`. | Database & ORM, Architecture | [bug-patterns/database-orm.md](bug-patterns/database-orm.md#bp-441) |
| BP-443 | Apache AGE Cypher node alias `end` causes `PostgresSyntaxError: syntax error at or near "end"` — `end` is a reserved keyword in both PostgreSQL and Apache AGE. Using it as a Cypher node alias (e.g., `MATCH (start)-[*2..5]-(end:entity)`) silently fails on every query execution, making the entire worker non-functional. Symptom: every job in `path_insight_jobs` gets marked `failed` with the AGE syntax error; the worker container accumulates restart-loop restarts (6 seen in practice) because it dies on a fatal Postgres connection error. The jobs are never progressed so `path_insights` stays empty. Fix: rename the destination node alias to a non-reserved word (`tgt`, `dest`, `n2`) throughout the Cypher MATCH, WHERE, and RETURN clauses. Regression test: assert `"end:entity" not in _CYPHER_FIND_PATHS`. Detection: any Cypher query that uses `end`, `begin`, `start`, `set`, `match`, `return`, `where`, `order`, `limit`, `skip`, `with`, `as`, `in`, `is`, `not`, `and`, `or`, `xor`, `true`, `false`, `null` as node/relationship aliases will fail with a syntax error under AGE. Reference: `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/infrastructure/age/path_discovery.py` (PLAN-0088 SA-5, 2026-05-10). | Database & ORM, Knowledge Graph | knowledge-graph |
| BP-442 | `BaseKafkaConsumer.ConsumerConfig.to_dict()` must propagate **every** rdkafka property the consumer relies on, including `partition.assignment.strategy` and `max.poll.records`. The pre-fix dict dropped both, so rdkafka silently fell back to its defaults: the `range` assignor (stop-the-world rebalance) and a 500-record batch. Combined with a slow handler (e.g. 30-60 s per message in the nlp-pipeline article consumer), this produced a "wedged consumer" pattern: the consumer-group `--describe` output showed all 12 partitions listed under the single member, but several partitions kept `CURRENT-OFFSET = -` for hours and the container went silent without crashing or rebalancing. Fix (PLAN-0087 D-P3-006/D-P3-009): added `partition_assignment_strategy: str = "cooperative-sticky"` to `ConsumerConfig`, included `max.poll.records` in `to_dict()`, and hopped the blocking `_record_consumer_lag` broker reads onto `run_in_executor(None, ...)` so they cannot delay the asyncio event loop (12 partitions × 1s timeout = up to 12s of blocking after every commit). `cooperative-sticky` performs incremental rebalances (KIP-429) so a slow consumer joining only revokes the partitions that need to move, instead of dropping every partition during the rebalance window. Detection: any consumer-group `--describe` output where `CURRENT-OFFSET = -` persists for > 1 hour while the consumer claims the partition is the canonical symptom; correlate with a quiet container log. Status: FIXED. Reference: `libs/messaging/src/messaging/kafka/consumer/base.py:79-127` and `libs/messaging/tests/unit/kafka/consumer/test_consumer_config.py`. | Kafka & Messaging | [bug-patterns/kafka.md](bug-patterns/kafka.md#bp-442) |
| BP-444 | Tool factory `entity_context` never wired from orchestrator — when a chat pipeline resolves entities in step N and builds a `ToolExecutor` in step N+1, the `entity_context` argument MUST be explicitly passed to `for_request()`. If omitted (even accidentally), every entity-scoped tool handler has a guard `if self._entity_context is not None:` that silently returns `[]`. The LLM sees empty tool results, triggers the `all_tools_failed` guard, and the user receives a generic fallback message ("Unable to retrieve relevant data") regardless of how rich the underlying data is. The resolver runs successfully but its output is thrown away. Detection: grep for `.for_request(` in orchestrators and confirm `entity_context=` is in the kwargs; also grep for `no_entity_context` warning logs at the tool level — if it appears on user queries, the wiring is broken. Fix: after entity resolution, build `EntityContext(entity_id=primary.entity_id, ticker=…)` and pass it. Also inject resolved entity UUIDs into the system prompt for cross-entity queries. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0088 night fix pass, 2026-05-10). Reference: `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/use_cases/chat_orchestrator.py`. | ML & LLM, API & Contracts | rag-chat |
| BP-445 | `InternalJWTMiddleware` `CRITICAL` log level in `skip_verification=True` mode fires on every authenticated request in dev — the middleware was logging `logger.critical("internal_jwt_unverified_decode", ...)` on each request decode when `skip_verification=True` (i.e. in all dev/local environments). This floods structured logs with false-positive CRITICALs, masking real alerts and making on-call triage impossible. The startup banner (logged once in `__init__`) should be `logger.warning` (appropriate severity for a configuration risk); the per-request decode path should be `logger.debug` (not observable at normal log level). Detection: any service whose logs show `internal_jwt_unverified_decode` at CRITICAL level is misconfigured — this is dev mode only and should never reach CRITICAL. Fix: change `__init__` banner to `logger.warning` and `dispatch` decode path to `logger.debug`. Status: FIXED (market-data SA-5 2026-05-10 second pass; rag-chat SA-1 night fix pass). Reference: `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/infrastructure/middleware/internal_jwt.py`, same pattern in all services. | Auth & Security, Observability | all services |
| BP-446 | APScheduler interval jobs without `next_run_time` wait a full interval before first execution — `scheduler.add_job(fn, "interval", seconds=N)` by default schedules the first run at `now + N` seconds. For workers with long intervals (60-120 min for embedding refresh), this means the feature is effectively broken for an hour after every service restart — narratives, definitions, and embeddings don't refresh, KG graph stays stale, AGE sync doesn't fire. The pattern is: short-critical jobs should use `next_run_time=datetime.now(tz=UTC) + timedelta(seconds=120)` to fire shortly after boot. Detection: search for `scheduler.add_job` calls without `next_run_time=` in scheduler files — any job that should fire "soon after startup" is a candidate. Fix: add `next_run_time=now+120s` to `definition_embedding`, `narrative_embedding`, `fundamentals_embedding`, and `age_sync` jobs. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0088 SA-3, 2026-05-10). Reference: `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/infrastructure/scheduler/scheduler.py`. | Workers & Schedulers | knowledge-graph |
| BP-447 | S9 proxy stripping valid backend query params based on stale comment — `proxy.py` can accumulate "WHY strip X param" comments that were written when the downstream service did NOT support param X, but become wrong after the service is updated. Symptom: a backend service gains a feature (e.g., `depth: int` for AGE Cypher traversal in knowledge-graph), but S9 silently drops the param because a comment says "service ignores it". The frontend never benefits from the new feature. Detection: for every `if "param" in raw_params: s7_params["param"] = …` pattern in proxy.py, verify the downstream service actually handles that param. For every param explicitly OMITTED with a "WHY strip" comment, re-verify the backend doc/source still lacks the param. Fix: add `depth: int = Query(default=1)` to S9's `get_entity_graph` route signature and forward it in the params dict. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0088 SA-4, 2026-05-10). | BP-448 | NLP pipeline emits `"regulatory_action"` temporal event type that violates the `ck_temporal_event_type` DB check constraint — the S7 KG consumer inserts `temporal_event_type` verbatim from the Kafka payload. | BP-449 | Global alias unique index not handled by `ON CONFLICT` clause + asyncpg type mismatch in KG provisional retry SQL — two bugs in the same consumer: (1) `EntityAliasRepository.insert()` targets only the per-entity partial unique index via `ON CONFLICT (entity_id, normalized_alias_text, alias_type) WHERE is_active = true`, but a second GLOBAL index `uidx_entity_aliases_normalized` on `(normalized_alias_text) WHERE alias_type = 'EXACT'` is NOT handled — a competing entity holding the same EXACT alias causes `UniqueViolationError` that escapes the conflict clause. Fix: wrap the INSERT in `begin_nested()` SAVEPOINT and catch `pgcode=23505` inside `insert()` itself — returns None on any conflict (per-entity OR global). Nested SAVEPOINTs are transparent to callers that already use their own `begin_nested()`. (2) `provisional_enrichment_core.py:apply_retry_transition()` CASE expression with `NULL` branch and `ELSE :base_now + interval` branch causes asyncpg `DatatypeMismatchError` — asyncpg infers `:base_now` as `interval` from the `+ interval` context. Fix: `CAST(:base_now AS timestamptz)`. Status: FIXED (2026-05-11). | BP-450 | AGE Cypher `WHERE ALL(rel IN r WHERE ...)` syntax invalid for variable-length relationship lists — AGE 1.5.0 does not support iterating over `r` (the multi-hop relationship bind variable) directly with `ALL()`. Only `relationships(path)` on a named path variable works. Using `MATCH (a)-[r*1..N]-(b) WHERE ALL(rel IN r WHERE ...)` causes `PostgresSyntaxError` on every depth≥2 request. Symptom: `GET /v1/entities/{id}/graph?depth=2` returns 500 `internal_error`; Intelligence tab shows 0 nodes/0 edges at depth≥2 despite the depth param now being correctly forwarded. Fix: `MATCH path = (center:entity …)-[r*1..N]-(neighbor:entity) WHERE ALL(rel IN relationships(path) WHERE …)`. Reference implementation: `cypher_path.py` uses `relationships(path)` correctly. Status: FIXED (2026-05-11). | BP-457 | `EntityAliasRepository.fuzzy_search` uses `%%` instead of `%` for pg_trgm operator — raises `UndefinedFunctionError: operator does not exist: character varying %% text`. In SQLAlchemy `text()`, `%` is NOT a Python format placeholder and needs no escaping. `%%` is sent literally to PostgreSQL as two percent signs, which is not a valid operator. The pg_trgm operator is single `%`. Additionally, asyncpg infers `:query` as `text` type — add `CAST(:query AS varchar)`. Prevention: never use `%%` in SQLAlchemy `text()` strings; always single `%` for pg_trgm. Status: FIXED (2026-05-11). | BP-458 | Hardcoded pixel-width `<div>` footer beneath AG Grid misaligns when TICKER column is pinned left, when user resizes columns, or when grid scrolls horizontally — AG Grid's pinned-left column container renders separately from the main scrollable viewport (two sibling DOM containers). | BP-460 | SEC EDGAR EFTS API field names mismatch — the legacy adapter code read `accession_no`, `cik`, and `file_name` from EFTS responses, but the live EFTS search-index API uses `adsh` (accession number), `ciks` (list of zero-padded CIK strings), and `period_ending`/`file_date` (no `period_of_report`). | BP-461 | **Two combined bugs broke AGE Cypher path discovery.** (1) AGE 1.5.0 does NOT support Cypher list comprehensions with `|` — `[n IN nodes(path) | n]` raises `PostgresSyntaxError: syntax error at or near "|"` at PREPARE time. Also NOT supported: `shortestPath()`, `allShortestPaths()`, `ALL(rel IN relationships(...) WHERE ...)`. CONFIRMED WORKING: `MATCH p = (s)-[*1..N]-(t) RETURN nodes(p), relationships(p) ORDER BY length(p) LIMIT N`. (2) `_parse_agtype_text()` used `rfind("::")` which only stripped the LAST `::` occurrence — for multi-element agtype arrays (e.g. `[{...}::vertex, {...}::vertex]`) this left inner `::vertex`/`::edge` annotations intact, causing `json.loads` to fail and returning empty paths even when AGE found results. Fix: replace `rfind("::")` with `re.sub(r'([}\\]])::[ \\t]*\\w+', r'\\1', text_val)` to strip ALL per-element type annotations. With both fixes AGE Cypher works end-to-end: Apple→Anthropic returns 5 paths (2 direct at confidence 1.0, 3 via intermediate nodes) in ~285ms. Detection: `POST /api/v1/graph/cypher/path` returns empty `paths_found=0` despite AGE having graph data; or HTTP 500 with `PostgresSyntaxError`. Status: FIXED (2026-05-11). Reference: `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/application/use_cases/cypher_path.py`. | Knowledge Graph, Database & ORM | knowledge-graph |

| BP-465 | Stale test mock HTTP method after implementation refactor — `TypeError: '>=' not supported between instances of 'AsyncMock' and 'int'`. | BP-466 | Multi-turn agent loop `max_iterations` causes `assert_called_once()` to fail on tool-executor mock — in `ChatOrchestratorUseCase`, the agent loop runs up to `max_iterations=8` times, calling `executor.execute_all()` once per iteration that contains tool calls. Any test then asserting `executor.execute_all.assert_called_once()` fails with `AssertionError: Expected 'execute_all' to be called once. Called 8 times.`. Fix: give the `chat_with_tools` mock a `side_effect` list: first element is the tool-calling response (exercises the dispatch path), second element is a direct-answer response (breaks the loop). `AsyncMock(side_effect=[llm_response, _make_tool_response_direct_answer()])`. Prevention: any test of a retry/loop that mocks the loop-continuation signal (tool calls) MUST also include a terminal response in the side_effect list that breaks the loop, unless the test is explicitly asserting loop-iteration count. | BP-467 | Ruff F841 lint-prefix suppression propagates `_` to downstream usages — when ruff auto-fixes an "unused local variable" warning by renaming `repos = ...` to `_repos = ...` (F841 suppression), it only renames the assignment site. All subsequent usages of `repos` in the same scope become `NameError: name 'repos' is not defined` at runtime. Symptom: tests fail with `NameError` on a variable that clearly exists two lines earlier; the renamed assignment is invisible unless you grep the exact assignment line. Fix: either rename all usages too (use IDE rename, not ruff auto-fix) or suppress via `# noqa: F841` at the assignment without renaming. Prevention: never apply `ruff --fix` to F841 in isolation; always review the diff to confirm the renamed variable has no downstream usages. | BP-470 | `InternalJWTMiddleware.startup()` raises `RuntimeError` when no api-gateway is in the compose profile, causing uvicorn to exit with code 3 — the middleware fetches the JWKS public key from `{api_gateway_url}/internal/jwks` at startup. | BP-480 | Rate-limit bypass when `request.state.user` is absent — S9 `RateLimitMiddleware` originally checked `if user and user.get("user_id")` against `getattr(request.state, "user", None)`, but a code path in `OIDCAuthMiddleware` that exited before any `request.state.user = None` assignment (e.g. unexpected exception before the dev-mode/real-OIDC branch) left the attribute UNSET. The `getattr` default papered over the missing attribute and the request silently fell through to the per-IP bucket (`rl:v1:ip:<sha256>`) — and on shared NAT/proxy infra (corporate networks, mobile carriers) one 20-req/min counter is shared across hundreds of unauthenticated users, enabling effective rate-limit bypass for brute-force probes that target the per-user bucket. Prevention: any middleware that depends on a request.state attribute set by an upstream middleware should (a) ensure the upstream sets it as the FIRST action of dispatch, (b) read via `getattr(..., default)`, and (c) log a defensive warning if the attribute is missing. Status: FIXED (2026-05-19; BUG-004, TASK-W1-04). | BP-488 | Idempotency dedup tables grow monotonically without a retention worker — `libs/messaging` `BaseKafkaConsumer.is_duplicate()` writes one row to `processed_events` per successfully consumed event so that operator-driven Kafka offset rewinds (and rebalance replays) are dropped. The original schema (`services/content-store/alembic/versions/0003_add_processed_events.py`) included a `processed_at` btree index but NO TTL job, NO scheduled DELETE, and no consumer of that index. At ~1M events/day this table accumulates ~30M rows/month/DB — eventually causing disk pressure, btree degradation (the partial index `idx_processed_events_processed_at` stops being efficient when 99% of the table predates the cutoff), and slow consumer startup. The Postgres-specific gotcha: `DELETE ... LIMIT N` is not supported, so a naive cleanup that issues `DELETE FROM processed_events WHERE processed_at < cutoff` will scan and lock the entire dead set in one statement — taking long-lived row locks that block the live consumer's `INSERT INTO processed_events` (which is part of the consumer's UoW). Fix: a shared `ProcessedEventsCleanupWorker` (`libs/messaging/src/messaging/kafka/maintenance/processed_events_cleanup.py`) that issues `DELETE ... WHERE event_id IN (SELECT event_id ... LIMIT N FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED)` in batches (default 10k, default retention 30 days), committing between batches and yielding to the event loop. `FOR UPDATE SKIP LOCKED` is critical so the cleanup never blocks the live consumer's insert; the consumer holds a row lock on its own `event_id` while its UoW is open, and we deliberately skip those — they will be picked up on the next scheduled run. Prevention: every belt-and-suspenders idempotency / audit / dedup table needs a documented retention policy AND a scheduled enforcement job at creation time — not retrofitted after the table is multi-million rows. Status: FIXED (2026-05-20; LIB-001, TASK-W1-06). Reference: `libs/messaging/src/messaging/kafka/maintenance/processed_events_cleanup.py`, `libs/messaging/tests/unit/kafka/maintenance/test_processed_events_cleanup.py` (5 unit tests), `services/content-store/alembic/versions/0003_add_processed_events.py` (table + index). Note: only S5 content-store currently materialises `processed_events` (other services dedup in Valkey via `ValkeyDedupConsumer`). | Messaging, Database & ORM | messaging |
| BP-489 | URL tracking-parameter strip list incomplete for socially-shared news URLs — S5 content-store Stage B normalized-hash dedup (`stage_b_normalized.py::normalize_url`) strips a hard-coded subset of UTM-style query params before hashing. The original `_TRACKING_PARAMS` frozenset covered Google/Facebook/Microsoft ad-click ids and the five UTM keys, but missed common modern social/email-share trackers: `_ga`/`_gl` (Google Analytics cross-domain linker), `_hsenc`/`_hsmi` (HubSpot email engagement), `igshid` (Instagram share id), `oly_anon_id`/`oly_enc_id` (Omeda), `wickedid`, `vero_id`/`vero_conv`, `yclid` (Yandex Ads), `s_cid` (Adobe SiteCatalyst). | BP-487 | Background-worker race across replicas double-counts holdings between activity-replay and snapshot-reconcile — S1 `BrokerageTransactionSyncWorker.sync_cycle()` loaded the active `BrokerageConnection` rows and iterated them one-by-one with no per-connection lock. Two worker replicas (or any concurrent re-entrant call to `_sync_connection` for the same connection_id) would both fetch the same SnapTrade activity window and both call `RecordTransactionUseCase` for the same `external_ref` values. The use case's `idempotency` table prevents the SECOND replica's insert from succeeding, but only AFTER the first replica's UoW has committed — both replicas have already executed their `find_by_external_ref()` dedup check by then and both go on to write. Net result: brief (5-60s) double-counted holdings before the final `_sync_holdings_from_snapshot()` upsert reconciles to broker-truth. If the snapshot fetch then fails (SnapTrade transient outage, account-positions endpoint 5xx), the drift persists for an entire 4h sync cycle. The dedup-via-idempotency-table pattern is necessary but NOT sufficient for write-side serialization across replicas — it deduplicates on individual rows, not on the entire per-connection sync session. Fix: wrap `_sync_connection` body in a per-connection PostgreSQL advisory lock via `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock(:key)` where `:key` is `int.from_bytes(hashlib.blake2b(str(connection_id).encode(), digest_size=8).digest(), "big") & 0x7FFF_FFFF_FFFF_FFFF` — non-blocking (`pg_try_*` returns false instead of queueing), transaction-scoped (auto-released on COMMIT/ROLLBACK so a crashed worker never strands the lock), deterministic across replicas (blake2b — NEVER Python's built-in `hash()` which is randomized per process when `PYTHONHASHSEED` is unset). The lock holds an outer UoW open for the duration of the per-connection sync (multiple inner UoWs still open/close per BP-057's "no SnapTrade calls while a write UoW is open" rule); the outer UoW does no writes and rolls back on exit, releasing the lock. Losing replicas log `brokerage_sync_skipped_lock_held` and return — the next 4h cycle picks the connection back up. Prevention: every worker that iterates a candidate set and performs multi-step external-API + write workflows needs per-candidate locking, NOT just row-level dedup tables. Row dedup catches duplicate INSERTs after the fact; advisory locks prevent the duplicate work from being started. Status: FIXED (2026-05-20; BUG-003, TASK-W1-03). Reference: `services/portfolio/src/portfolio/workers/brokerage_sync_worker.py:81-139` (`_connection_lock_key` + `_try_acquire_connection_lock` helpers), `services/portfolio/src/portfolio/workers/brokerage_sync_worker.py:273-301` (`_sync_connection` lock scope), `services/portfolio/tests/unit/test_worker_brokerage_sync.py` (4 regression tests: key determinism, key uniqueness, same-connection serialization, different-connection parallelism). | Database & ORM, Messaging | portfolio |
| BP-486 | Background-worker candidate query missing routing-tier filter creates feedback-loop noise — S6 `ArticleImpactWindowRepository.get_articles_needing_windows()` selected ALL articles with resolved financial-instrument mentions older than `min_age_hours`, including SUPPRESS-tier (`ProcessingPath.HALT`) documents. The price-impact labelling worker would then compute t0/t1/t2/t5 window scores for low-quality articles, and those impact scores fed back into the composite routing score for any future article citing the same instrument — a noise-amplifying feedback loop that biases routing decisions toward suppressed-article instruments. The CTE filtered on `entity_mentions` and `document_source_metadata` but never JOINed `routing_decisions`, so suppression-gate decisions were invisible to the worker. The NULL fallback is critical: `processing_path` was added in migration 0015 and legacy rows are NULL; a bare `!= 'halt'` would silently drop them due to SQL three-valued logic (`NULL != 'halt'` → NULL → false). Prevention: any background-worker candidate-set query MUST consult the routing/suppression decision tables — pipeline-level gates on emission (BP-485) are not sufficient if a downstream worker pulls candidates independently via its own query.
