| BP-459 | Partial unique index `WHERE entity_type != 'financial_instrument'` on `canonical_entities(lower(canonical_name))` allows phantom duplicate entities — a new provisional entity whose LLM-produced canonical name is a variation of an existing `financial_instrument` (e.g., "Amazon Business" vs "Amazon Inc.") is inserted as a fresh row because the conflict detection index excludes all `financial_instrument` rows. Compounded by: the `ProvisionalEnrichmentWorker` LLM extraction step has no pre-insert lookup against existing canonicals, and the `class_aware_canonical_match()` fuzzy matcher (PLAN-0087, used by S8 RAG) is never called during S7 enrichment. Symptom: two nodes for the same company appear in the entity graph; relations may be attached to the phantom node; entity search returns duplicates. Fix: (1) make the unique index unconditional (remove the `WHERE` predicate), handle entity_type coalescing in the `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE` clause; (2) call `class_aware_canonical_match()` before provisional entity insertion — reuse existing entity if match confidence exceeds threshold; (3) one-off data cleanup: delete phantom rows and re-point their relations. Detection: `SELECT lower(canonical_name), count(*) FROM canonical_entities GROUP BY lower(canonical_name) HAVING count(*) > 1`. Status: OPEN (2026-05-11). Reference: `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/infrastructure/intelligence_db/repositories/canonical_entity.py:create_or_get`, `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/infrastructure/workers/provisional_enrichment_core.py`. | Database & ORM, Knowledge Graph | knowledge-graph |
| BP-491 | All source-adapter poll loops fire on the same wall-clock instant when they share a single `interval_seconds` and start at the same moment — S4 content-ingestion `IngestionScheduler` schedules one `asyncio.Task` per enabled source (EODHD, SEC EDGAR, Finnhub, NewsAPI). Each task entered its `while self._running:` loop immediately and the first `await self._run_fn(source)` ran inside the same event-loop iteration for all four. Subsequent ticks then used a shared `await asyncio.sleep(self._interval_seconds)` with no per-source offset, so the four sources stayed phase-locked forever. On every 15-minute boundary the scheduler would emit four simultaneous outbound HTTP fetches + four DB writes + four Kafka publishes, producing a recurring CPU/network spike (a classic thundering herd). The spike was invisible at small scale but compounded with consumer lag at scale, and made backpressure/rate-limit tuning per source impossible because they never observed each other in isolation. Fix: a deterministic-by-source-name startup offset, `_startup_offset_seconds(name, interval) = int(md5(name).hexdigest(),16) % max(1, interval//4)`, awaited ONCE at the top of `_poll_loop` before the first `run_fn` call. md5 (with `usedforsecurity=False`) is intentional — collision resistance is irrelevant, only deterministic spread matters. The offset is stable across restarts so a given source always lands in the same slot of the interval window; subsequent ticks remain at the full `interval_seconds` (no per-tick jitter — only startup phase). Prevention: any scheduler that launches N parallel periodic tasks with a shared interval MUST stagger their first tick by a deterministic per-task offset (hash of task identity), NEVER use `random.random()` (non-deterministic across restarts → operator confusion) and NEVER use Python's built-in `hash()` (randomized per process unless `PYTHONHASHSEED` is set). Status: FIXED (2026-05-19; BUG-008, TASK-W2-03). Reference: `services/content-ingestion/src/content_ingestion/infrastructure/scheduler/scheduler.py:28-46,134-143` (`_startup_offset_seconds` helper + `_poll_loop` integration), `services/content-ingestion/tests/unit/test_scheduler_jitter.py` (6 unit tests: 4-source distinctness, determinism, zero/one/negative interval boundaries). | Messaging | content-ingestion |
| BP-490 | WebSocket session retains a stale JWT for the lifetime of the connection, never re-checking expiry after handshake — S10 alert `alerts_stream` validates the ws-token at the HTTP upgrade (PyJWT enforces `exp` once at decode time) and then enters an `async with valkey.subscribe(channel) as pubsub: while True: ...` dispatch loop that can live for hours. ws-tokens issued by S9 `issue_ws_jwt` are deliberately short-lived (60-300 s) to limit blast radius if leaked, but the alert handler kept sending alerts to the client long after `exp` had passed because nothing in the loop re-checked the token. Two compounding silent-failure paths: (1) the dispatch loop's cleanup branch — `try: send_json + close; except Exception: pass # noqa: S110` — swallowed every error during teardown, so connection-close failures never surfaced; (2) the loop only exited on `WebSocketDisconnect` or on a `valkey.subscribe` exception, so the only thing that could kick an expired session was the client disconnecting first. Net effect: a leaked ws-token continued receiving alerts indefinitely. Fix: (a) capture `token_exp: int = int(payload["exp"])` after the handshake decode (the `require=["exp"]` option guarantees the claim is present); (b) before EVERY send in the dispatch loop, check `if time.time() >= token_exp: try: send_json({"type":"auth_expired", "message":"Session token expired"}) except Exception: pass; await close(code=4401); return`; the inner suppress is intentional (peer may already be gone) but is followed unconditionally by `close()` so the loop always terminates; (c) replace the cleanup-branch `except Exception: pass` with `except Exception as exc: logger.warning("websocket_dispatch_error", user_id=..., error=str(exc), exc_info=False)` — the swallow stays (disconnect noise during teardown is expected) but the event is now observable. Prevention: any long-lived authenticated session (WebSocket, SSE, gRPC bidi) MUST re-check the token expiry on every dispatch — single-check-at-handshake is only safe for request/response. And any bare `except Exception: pass` in a network teardown path should be a structlog warning, not silent. Status: FIXED (2026-05-19; BUG-007, TASK-W2-02). Reference: `services/alert/src/alert/api/routes.py:495-578` (token_exp capture + dispatch-loop expiry check + observable cleanup), `services/alert/tests/unit/api/test_alerts_api.py::TestWebSocketMidStreamExpiry` (2 regression tests: mid-stream expiry emits `auth_expired` + close 4401; cleanup-branch error emits `websocket_dispatch_error` log). | Auth & Security | alert |
| BP-492 | Domain event lacked an `is_backfill` flag, so downstream consumers could not distinguish live data from a historical replay — S2 market-ingestion `MarketDatasetFetched` (`services/market-ingestion/.../domain/events.py`) shipped 27 Avro fields covering provider/symbol/timeframe/refs but no flag indicating whether the producing task was a backfill. The producer knew the value (the DB layer already wrote `is_backfill = task.range_start is not None` on the `ingestion_tasks` row in `task_repository.py:83`) but the value was dropped at the event boundary. Symptom: when an operator triggered a backfill of historical quotes, S3 market-data `QuotesConsumer` invalidated the Valkey quote cache and warmed the `PriceSnapshotCache` with each historical bar — the live "last price" used by S10 alert evaluation and the frontend ticker would be overwritten with a stale price from the backfill window, tripping price-threshold alerts on data the user never actually traded against. Fix (BUG-009 / TASK-W2-04): (1) append `is_backfill: boolean = false` to `infra/kafka/schemas/market.dataset.fetched.avsc` — appending with a literal default is R11-safe so older consumers still decode old payloads; (2) add `is_backfill: bool = False` to the `MarketDatasetFetched` frozen kw-only dataclass plus its `to_dict` / `from_dict` (defaulting to False on missing key for forward-compat); (3) thread the flag through both `messaging/mapper.py` and `messaging/kafka/mapper.py`; (4) at the producer site (`pipeline.py`) derive the flag exactly like `task_repository` does — `is_backfill = task.range_start is not None` — to keep the wire payload, the DB row, and the dedupe-key contract in lock-step (any drift between these three is itself a footgun); (5) in `QuotesConsumer.process_message`, gate the live-cache hot-paths (`QuoteCache.invalidate`, `PriceSnapshotCache.set`) on `not is_backfill` — DB upsert still runs so historical rows are durably stored, but the live signal stays clean. Prevention: any cross-service event whose downstream actions include cache fan-out, alert evaluation, or websocket push MUST carry an explicit "is this real-time?" flag at the schema boundary; never let consumers infer it from secondary fields like `range_start` (a backfill of a single intraday window can legitimately set range_start to "today" and look live). Always append the flag with a forward-compat default so the producer and consumer can be upgraded independently. Status: FIXED (2026-05-20; BUG-009, TASK-W2-04). Reference: `services/market-ingestion/src/market_ingestion/domain/events.py:55-100`, `services/market-ingestion/src/market_ingestion/application/use_cases/strategies/pipeline.py:380-410`, `services/market-data/src/market_data/infrastructure/messaging/consumers/quotes_consumer.py:282-340`, `infra/kafka/schemas/market.dataset.fetched.avsc`. | Messaging, Cache | market-ingestion, market-data |

| BP-494 | Bash process substitution in Makefile recipe silently fails under `/bin/sh` — Make recipes execute under `SHELL := /bin/sh` (dash on macOS, posix on Linux); `<(...)` and `>(...)` are bash-only. In `make seed-verify-m017` the line `MISSING=$$(comm -23 <(echo "$$ENTITIES") <(echo "$$INSTRUMENTS"))` errored with `syntax error near unexpected token '('` but the error was inside a `$$()` substitution so `MISSING=""` and the downstream `[ "$$N_MISS" -gt 0 ]` evaluated false → "M-017 OK" printed regardless of actual state. The target silently lied about the M-017 invariant for the entire PRD-0089 F2 wave. Fix: rewrite using temp files (`mktemp` + `comm <file1> <file2>` + `trap rm -f ... EXIT`), sh-compatible; also narrow the SELECT to `entity_id::text LIKE '0190%'` so legacy v4-UUID rows from migration 0009 don't falsely violate. Prevention: lint Makefile recipes for bash-isms — `grep -E '<\(\|>\(\|\[\[' Makefile` should be empty, or every match wrapped under `bash -c`. A Makefile-wide `SHELL := /bin/bash` is a heavier alternative; the F2 cleanup deliberately picked the surgical rewrite to avoid changing semantics in other targets. Status: FIXED (2026-05-20; PRD-0089 F2 cleanup). Reference: `Makefile:225-258` (seed-verify-m017 target). | Config & Docker | (Makefile) |

| BP-496 | Pure helper placed in `infrastructure/` and imported from `application/` — `tests/architecture/test_layer_boundaries.py` enforces the hexagonal invariant `LAYER-APP-ISOLATION` (application/ may only depend on domain/ and ports). | BP-497 | TanStack query-key consumer drift after factory introduction — a central `qk.*` factory was added in `apps/worldview-web/lib/query/keys.ts` (PRD-0089 W1 plan §5 explicitly promised `qk.portfolios.list() (existing)` so consumers would dedup), but the migration of legacy bare-key consumers never happened. | BP-502 | PostgreSQL `max_connections` not tuned for multi-container topology — the platform grew from 1 service to 10 services + 44 worker containers against a single PostgreSQL instance that retains the compile-time default of `max_connections=100`. With 55 DB-connected containers and standard pool configs (pool_size=10/20, max_overflow=20/30 per container, two engines per dual-DB service), the theoretical maximum connection count exceeds 3,000. At rest the platform was observed at 101/100 connections, causing intermittent `FATAL: too many clients already` errors that blocked non-critical operations (e.g. ETF seeding via psql, admin queries). 99/101 connections showed `application_name=''` making diagnosis impossible. Root cause: `docker-compose.yml` postgres service had no `command:` override and no `postgresql.conf`; all defaults were used. Fix: add `command: postgres -c max_connections=500 -c shared_buffers=256MB` to the postgres service in docker-compose.yml; add `connect_args={"server_settings": {"application_name": "<service>"}}` and `pool_recycle=300` to all session factories (9 services missing it; `alert` had the pattern already). Prevention: when adding any new DB-connected service or worker to the compose stack, verify `total_containers × avg_pool_max < max_connections × 0.8`. Document the capacity math in `infra/postgres/README.md` or a similar infra note. Status: FIXED (2026-05-21). Reference: `infra/compose/docker-compose.yml:postgres.command`, all `services/*/infrastructure/*/session.py` files. | Infrastructure, Config | all services |
| BP-499 | `HttpInstrumentLookupClient` called a removed S2 route — the client used `GET /api/v1/instruments/symbol/{symbol}` (path-param form) which was deleted from S2 during the F2 redesign. | BP-500 | Holdings wiped when ALL broker positions fail instrument resolution — `_sync_holdings_from_snapshot` iterated broker positions, attempted to resolve each symbol via S2, and passed the `resolved` list to `UpsertHoldingsFromSnapshotUseCase`. The use case correctly interprets "position present in broker snapshot but absent from resolved list = closed position" and deletes those holdings. User-visible symptom: portfolio page showed "No positions tracked yet / Connect a brokerage" after a successful brokerage connection and sync. | BP-501 | FEE and INTEREST brokerage activities raised `UNSUPPORTED_TYPE` sync errors — `_process_activity` looked up the SnapTrade `activity_type` in `_TYPE_MAP`; FEE and INTEREST were absent (cash-only activities: no instrument_id). A `KeyError` was caught and recorded as `SyncErrorType.UNSUPPORTED_TYPE` for each such transaction, creating junk sync-error rows that the user sees as "Unsupported activity type: 'INTEREST'" or "'FEE'" in the brokerage panel. Root cause: `instrument_id` is `NOT NULL` on the `transactions` table and `RecordTransactionCommand.instrument_id: UUID` is required — there is no path to persist a cash-only transaction without a schema change. The correct behavior is silent skip, not an error. Fix: (1) introduce `_CASH_ACTIVITY_TYPES: frozenset = frozenset({"FEE", "INTEREST"})` checked before `_TYPE_MAP` lookup; (2) return early with a Prometheus `status="skipped"` label — no sync error row is created; (3) add `TransactionType.INTEREST` to the domain enum so it is available when the schema constraint is relaxed in a future wave. Prevention: when a new activity type is encountered from an external broker API, explicitly decide: does it produce a DB row? If not, add it to `_CASH_ACTIVITY_TYPES` (or equivalent); never leave it to fall through to the "unsupported type" catch-all. Regression tests: `test_process_activity_fee_silently_skipped_no_sync_error`, `test_process_activity_interest_silently_skipped_no_sync_error` in `services/portfolio/tests/unit/test_worker_brokerage_sync.py`. | BP-503 | E2E mock URL mismatch — S9 gateway endpoint path diverges from mock pattern — when writing Playwright route mocks, the URL pattern must reflect the ACTUAL URL the browser client sends, not the backend service's internal sub-path. | BP-504 | E2E mock response format mismatch — frontend-shape vs wire-format — `getHoldings()` in the gateway returns a frontend `HoldingsResponse` object, but its `apiFetch` call receives the raw S1 wire format (`RawHolding[]` or `{items: RawHolding[]}`) and transforms it client-side. If an e2e mock returns the frontend-shaped object, the transformation code receives fields like `holdings: [...]` (not an array or items-envelope) and silently falls back to `[]`. The portfolio page then enters the "BrokerageEmptyState" path and never renders holdings data. Similarly, `getPortfolios()` expects `{items: [...], total, limit, offset}` from S9; the mock must use this S1 envelope shape, not the transformed `Portfolio[]` array. Prevention: for every gateway mock, read the `apiFetch<RawType>` type parameter in the source (the raw wire type), not the return type of the method (the transformed type). | BP-505 | TanStack Query stale cache across UTC midnight boundary — omitting a date-derived value from the query key causes the cache to serve yesterday's data for today's requests after midnight UTC. The user saw SPY bars from the previous calendar day for up to 30s after midnight — or indefinitely if the tab stayed open. | BP-507 | `useTopMovers` always returned empty contributors/detractors because it read `holding.unrealised_pnl_pct` which is permanently `null` — `getHoldings()` in `lib/api/portfolios.ts` transforms the raw S1 response into frontend `Holding` objects and explicitly sets `unrealised_pnl_pct: null` on every holding (price enrichment happens client-side from live quotes, not from S1). `useTopMovers` filtered holdings with `typeof h.unrealised_pnl_pct === "number"` which excluded all holdings since the field is always `null`. The result was always `{contributors: [], detractors: []}`, so `ContributorsStrip` permanently showed "—" for every entry regardless of how many holdings the portfolio had. Fix: replace `unrealised_pnl_pct` read with `livePriceFor(h, quotes)` (same function used by `computePortfolioKPI` in `kpi.ts`), computing `pnlPct = ((livePrice - h.average_cost) / h.average_cost) * 100`. Add `quotes: QuoteMap = {}` as the second parameter to `useTopMovers`; update the call site in `portfolio/page.tsx` to pass `holdingsQuotes`. When quotes haven't resolved yet, `livePriceFor` falls back to `average_cost` → `pnlPct=0` → excluded from both contributors and detractors, so the strip correctly shows "—" during the loading window. Prevention: when a hook derives a derived metric from a `Holding` field that is initialised as `null` client-side, check whether the enrichment step that populates it is reachable from the hook's data source. `unrealised_pnl_pct` on `Holding` is a "write-here" field populated only via the deprecated S1 enrichment path — use `livePriceFor(h, quotes)` + `average_cost` instead. | BP-510 | `ConcentrationSectorTeaseStrip` crashed the portfolio page when the concentration endpoint returned a partial/empty shape — the component called `conc.hhi.toFixed(0)` without a null guard. Pattern: `conc.hhi != null ? conc.hhi.toFixed(0) : "—"`. Status: FIXED (2026-05-21). | BP-511 | AG Grid `h-full` wrapper resolves to 0px height inside a page-level `overflow-y-auto` scroll container — AG Grid requires a non-zero, explicit container height to render rows into its virtual viewport. When `SemanticHoldingsTable` was wrapped in `<div className="flex flex-col overflow-auto relative">` (with no explicit height), `h-full` on the inner `AgGridBase` wrapper resolved to 0px because there was no ancestor with an explicit height in the scroll container chain. AG Grid rendered the header row and all row DOM nodes (168 cells visible to Playwright's `.ag-cell` locator) but clipped all rows to the 0px bounding box — the grid appeared as a 2px sliver in production. E2E tests passed because Playwright counts cells in the DOM overflow even at 0px visual height, but users saw only the header with no data rows. Fix: compute intrinsic height from row count: `gridHeight = Math.min(rowCount, MAX_VISIBLE_ROWS) * ROW_H + HEADER_H + PINNED_ROW_H` and apply as `style={{ height: "${gridHeight}px" }}` on the container div; remove `overflow-auto` from the container (grid manages its own overflow). Prevention: never use `h-full` or `flex-1` to size an AG Grid wrapper when any ancestor is an `overflow-y-auto` scroll container without an explicit height — the CSS height resolution chain breaks at the scroll container boundary. Always provide an explicit pixel or `calc()` height to the immediate AG Grid container. Status: FIXED (2026-05-21). Reference: `apps/worldview-web/components/portfolio/SemanticHoldingsTable.tsx:370-381`. | Frontend, CSS | apps/worldview-web |
| BP-509 | AG Grid `context` not threaded to cell renderers because `AgGridBase` had no `context` prop — `SparklineCellRenderer` reads sparkline data from `params.context.holdingsSeries` (keyed by ticker). Prevention: when a cell renderer reads from `params.context`, trace the full path from the data source → wrapper component → `AgGridBase` → `<AgGridReact context=…>` and verify the context object is threaded at every step. A cell renderer that reads an optional context field will silently render placeholder values when context is missing — there is no runtime error. Status: FIXED (2026-05-21). | BP-515 | Monitoring widget polling a delivery-queue table instead of the authoritative source table — `RecentAlerts` polled `GET /v1/alerts/pending` which reads the `pending_alerts` fan-out delivery queue. That table contains rows only while alerts are awaiting delivery to notification channels; once delivered (or for alerts seeded directly into `alerts`), it is empty. The `alerts` table had 2 rows but the widget always showed 0 results from REST. The correct endpoint for a read-only monitoring widget is `GET /v1/alerts/history` which queries the authoritative `alerts` table. | BP-516 | Instrument-page `useQuery` hooks missing `!!token` in `enabled` guard — auth-context race causes permanent error/unavailable state — Four instrument-page hooks (`useInstrumentBrief`, `useQuoteSidebarData`, `useMetricsTableData`, `useInstrumentBundle`) used `enabled: !!id` (or `!!entityId`) without gating on `!!token`. `ApiClientProvider` lives in the root layout and renders unconditionally; the auth gate in `(app)/layout.tsx` only prevents child rendering while `isLoading=true`. In React 18 concurrent mode the `ApiClientContext` value (`accessToken`) can be `null` on the first render batch before the auth context async initialization completes. During that window, all 4 hooks fire unauthenticated → 401 responses. `useInstrumentBrief` sets `retry: false`, so the query enters permanent error state and immediately triggers POST `/generate` with a null token → another 401 → `setStatus("unavailable")`. The other 3 hooks have default retry (3×), but once token arrives no automatic refetch occurs because the token is not in the `queryKey` — the stale successful cache entry (from a different session) or the errored entry (first load) stays served until manually invalidated. Symptom: AI brief always shows "Unavailable"; MetricsTable, QuoteSidebar, and page bundle show empty/skeleton state until a hard refresh on a warm cache session. Fix: add `!!token` to all `enabled` conditions: `enabled: !!instrumentId && !!token`. The codebase already provides `useAuthedQuery` which auto-disables on `null` token; prefer it for new hooks. Prevention: (1) any `useQuery` call that sends an `Authorization` header MUST include `!!token` in `enabled`; (2) prefer `useAuthedQuery` over raw `useQuery` for authenticated endpoints (it enforces this automatically); (3) when adding `retry: false` to a query, verify the `enabled` guard covers all cases that would fire a 401. Status: FIXED (2026-05-21). Reference: `apps/worldview-web/components/instrument/hooks/use*.ts`, `apps/worldview-web/lib/api-client.tsx:useAuthedQuery`. | Frontend, Auth | apps/worldview-web |

| BP-526 | `MagicMock()` used for async-awaited method creates coincidental fail-open via `TypeError` — when a `MagicMock()` is used for a method that is `await`ed (e.g. `valkey.get`), `await MagicMock()` raises `TypeError: object MagicMock can't be used in 'await' expression`. If the production code wraps the `await` in `except Exception`, the `TypeError` is caught as a coincidental fail-open: the code proceeds exactly as if the operation failed gracefully. Tests appear to exercise the fail-open path, but they are actually testing an internal mock error, not the intended production failure scenario (e.g. a real `ConnectionError`). This also means cache-hit vs cache-miss behaviour cannot be distinguished in tests — `mock_valkey.get = MagicMock(return_value=b"...")` never returns `b"..."` because the `await` raises before the mock's return value is read. Fix: always use `AsyncMock` for methods that will be `await`ed: `mock_valkey.get = AsyncMock(return_value=None)` for cache-miss, `AsyncMock(return_value=b"data")` for cache-hit, `AsyncMock(side_effect=ConnectionError())` for genuine fail-open. Prevention: any test fixture that creates a mock for an async method MUST use `AsyncMock`, not `MagicMock`. Grep for `MagicMock()` assignments where the method name is `await`ed in production code (e.g. `await client.get`, `await valkey.incr`). Status: FIXED (2026-05-22; F-QA-016). Reference: `services/api-gateway/tests/conftest.py:mock_valkey.*`, `services/api-gateway/tests/unit/api/routers/test_intelligence_proxy.py:test_intelligence_cache_*`. | Testing | api-gateway |

| BP-534 | LLM API call missing `asyncio.wait_for` wall-clock timeout causes consumer DLQ storm — `DeepSeekExtractionAdapter` used `httpx.Timeout(read=120s)` which is a per-chunk read timeout, not a total wall-clock timeout. When DeepInfra's TTFT (time-to-first-token) exceeds 120s under queue pressure, the timeout fires per-chunk but the `asyncio.timeout(300s)` watchdog in `BaseKafkaConsumer._handle_message()` fires first when GLiNER (50-60s) + extraction TTFT (250s) > 300s budget. 93 articles dead-lettered. | BP-537 | `useMutation` with `retry: N` retries ALL errors including 429 (rate limit) — unlike `useQuery`, TanStack Query's `useMutation` has no built-in 4xx filter. `retry: 3` on a POST mutation fires 4 identical requests in 7 seconds when S9 returns 429. The only way to exclude 4xx from mutation retries is a `shouldRetry` predicate: `retry: (count, err) => err instanceof GatewayError && err.status >= 500 && count < 3`. Mutations with `retry: N` and no `shouldRetry` guard fail silently (the user sees the eventual error after all retries exhaust) while amplifying load on rate-limited endpoints. Prevention: never set `retry: N` on a mutation without a `shouldRetry` guard; prefer a shared `shouldRetryOnServerError` helper from `lib/gateway.ts`. Status: OPEN (2026-05-23). | BP-544 | Apache AGE vlabel/elabel not pre-created → first INSERT raises `ProgrammingError: label "Article" does not exist` → generic `except Exception` catches it → consumer logs a warning and advances the Kafka watermark as if the write had succeeded. Hours of `relations` and entity rows accumulate in Postgres while AGE stays empty; downstream Cypher traversals operate on a near-empty graph and return zero-hop answers for every query. | BP-545 | `librdkafka` keeps a per-process DNS cache that pins broker hostnames to their resolved IPs at first connection; when Compose recreates the `kafka` container the IP changes but consumers keep dialing the dead address forever, silently stopping all message processing while metrics report "connected" because the underlying TCP socket has not failed yet. The `restart: unless-stopped` policy never triggers because the process is still alive. Fix: set `topic.metadata.refresh.interval.ms=30000` and `broker.address.ttl=30000` on every Kafka client; add a Compose `depends_on: { kafka: { condition: service_healthy } }` so a kafka restart cascades to consumers (R35); add a Prometheus alert on `kafka_consumer_lag` plateau without `messages_consumed` increase for >5min. | BP-546 | A repository `SELECT col_x, col_y FROM tbl` where `col_y` was renamed/removed in a later migration parses successfully (psycopg2/asyncpg only validates syntax client-side) and only fails at execution as `UndefinedColumn`. If the call site catches the exception generically the worker silently returns an empty result; if not, the error surfaces in production rather than CI because unit tests typically mock the repository. The production guard is: at service startup, run every repository's parameterized SELECT against `EXPLAIN (FORMAT JSON)` with dummy params and crash the process if the column set differs from the ORM model. The PLAN-0093 QA-1 P0 SQL bugs (entity_event_exposure singular table; provisional_entity_queue.updated_at; relation_summaries.subject_entity_id) are exact instances of this pattern in **test code** — three different developers wrote SELECTs against stale column names with no review catching it. Fix per-site: rename column in test/repo; add CI guard: `grep -rE "FROM (entity_event_exposure|relation_evidence)\b" tests/ services/` should match zero files (only plural/canonical names allowed). Prevention: every new repository SELECT must be exercised by an integration test that hits the real DB at least once. Status: FIXED for QA-1 P0s (2026-05-24; PLAN-0093 F-1). Reference: `tests/validation/test_age_coverage.py`, `tests/validation/test_enrichment_quality.py`, `tests/validation/test_relations_quality.py`. | Database & ORM, Testing | all |
| BP-547 | LLM agent receives a tool result with `N=1` row (e.g. a single price quote, a single revenue datum) and the prose answer extrapolates to a trend, range, or multi-period claim that the data does not support — "AMD's Q4 revenue was $7.66B, up from a strong Q3" when only Q4 was returned. The numeric-grounding validator passes because $7.66B IS in the tool corpus, but "up from a strong Q3" is unsupported. The PLAN-0093 E-2 fix added entity-tagged numeric pools (so AMD's $7.66B can't be claimed as NVDA's), but the **premise-check / pretraining-supplement** layer is still open as QA-2 P0-1: the LLM must refuse to answer questions whose premise (e.g. "Why did X acquire Y last quarter?") is not corroborated by any tool result. Fix: prepend `PREMISE CHECK` rule to `libs/prompts/src/prompts/chat/tool_use.py` (verbatim wording in PLAN-0093 Annex A.2); add forbidden clause "Accepting M&A/partnership/leadership claims from the user's question without tool confirmation"; add A10 regression question asserting refusal language. Prevention: any LLM agent loop whose system prompt does not explicitly forbid extrapolation beyond tool results will hallucinate (HR-064). Status: PARTIAL — entity-tagging FIXED (E-2, 2026-05-24); premise-refusal OPEN as QA-2 P0-1 (in-flight). Reference: `libs/prompts/src/prompts/chat/tool_use.py`, `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/validation/numeric_grounding.py`. | ML & LLM, API & Contracts | rag-chat |
| BP-548 | `canonical_entities.enrichment_attempts` is declared `int DEFAULT 0 NOT NULL` and queried by a partial index `WHERE enriched_at IS NULL AND enrichment_attempts < 5` to find work for `StructuredEnrichmentWorker`. The worker increments an in-memory counter on failure but never executes `UPDATE canonical_entities SET enrichment_attempts = enrichment_attempts + 1 WHERE entity_id = $1`. Result: the partial index keeps returning the same 1,790 rows every cycle (34% of canonical_entities), the worker churns through them at retry-cap speed, the dashboard shows "enrichment is running" because the worker process is alive, and no entity ever crosses the `enrichment_attempts >= 5` line. The watermark / scheduling state advances on each attempted batch — looks like a healthy partial-sync sweep. Fix: in the worker's failure path, `await uow.canonical_entities.bump_enrichment_attempts(entity_id)` BEFORE the catch returns; add a SQL backfill `UPDATE canonical_entities SET enrichment_attempts = (SELECT count(*) FROM provisional_entity_queue WHERE entity_id = ce.entity_id AND status='failed') WHERE enrichment_attempts = 0 AND enriched_at IS NULL`; add a regression test that calls the worker twice on a row and asserts the counter went up. Prevention: every counter referenced in a WHERE clause must have an explicit UPDATE call site — grep for `enrichment_attempts <` / `attempts <` and confirm a paired UPDATE exists (HR-065). Status: FIXED (2026-05-24; PLAN-0093 D-1). Reference: `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/infrastructure/workers/structured_enrichment.py`, F-DB-ENRICHMENT-001. | Workers & Schedulers, Database & ORM | knowledge-graph |
| BP-550 | RAG-chat orchestrator misclassified "tool returned empty" as "tool failed" — the all-tools-failed guard at iteration 0 only flipped `_all_failed = False` when `_count > 0`. A tool that succeeded (HTTP 200, no exception) but returned an empty list (e.g. `get_contradictions` for an entity whose `relation_contradiction_links` table is empty — true for ALL entities in the current dataset) would trigger the same `all_tools_failed` SSE error as a genuine tool crash. Q7 ("contradictions around Tesla") surfaced as USELESS verdict even though the agent had successfully reached S7 and gotten an honest "no rows" answer back. Fix (FIX-LIVE-Y, 2026-05-25): split `_all_failed` into two flags — `_all_failed` keeps legacy meaning (no useful data this round → still triggers fallback chain); new `_all_errored` is only True when every tool's `_item is None` (genuine crash). At iteration-0 all-fail check, if `not _all_errored` we now (1) emit `all_tools_returned_empty` info log, (2) inject the OpenAI-spec-required `assistant{tool_calls}` + `tool{tool_call_id}` placeholders so the next LLM turn doesn't reject with "missing required tool" (FIX-LIVE-J/R), (3) inject a `user` guidance message ("tools returned no data — answer honestly, do not call more tools"), (4) `continue` the loop. The next LLM turn produces a graceful MARGINAL answer ("I searched for contradictions but found none in the available data") instead of an opaque hard error. Side fix in same patch: when iteration > 0 ends with SUBSTANTIVE direct text (not just empty text+no-tools), set `_skip_final_stream=True` so the post-loop `stream_chat` at line ~1206 doesn't re-emit the same answer (was producing visible duplicates like "I searched for ... [A]. I searched for ... [B]."). Prevention: any code that aggregates per-tool outcomes must distinguish three states — `ok` / `empty` / `error` — and only the `error` aggregate may escalate to a hard-failure SSE; `empty` is a successful "no data" outcome that the LLM should answer honestly. Status: FIXED (2026-05-25; FIX-LIVE-Y). Reference: `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/use_cases/chat_orchestrator.py:817-870, 935-997`, regression tests `services/rag-chat/tests/unit/use_cases/test_chat_orchestrator_fallback.py::test_all_tools_errored_still_emits_all_tools_failed` + `::test_fallback_chain_exhaustion_falls_through_to_graceful_no_data`. | RAG & Tool Use | rag-chat |
| BP-549 | Migration leaves orphan downstream helpers. After an architecture migration (e.g. tool-use loop replaces fixed pipeline, Kafka consumer replaces APScheduler worker), the new upstream caller no longer references downstream helper classes, but the helpers + their unit tests + DI wiring survive. Type-check and tests pass because tests construct helpers directly; production never invokes them. Example: `GraphEnricher` + `FusionPipeline` in `services/rag-chat/` survived PLAN-0067's tool-use migration as dead code for ~6 months; deleted 2026-05-24 in audit `docs/audits/2026-05-24-investigation-graphenricher-dormant.md`. Same family also surfaced the same day: `AlphaVantageProviderAdapter` stub in `services/market-ingestion/.../adapters/providers/alpha_vantage.py` (never imported — the real fundamentals adapter lives in `infrastructure/external/`); three KG worker tombstones (`economic_events_worker.py` / `macro_indicator_worker.py` / `insider_transactions_worker.py`) replaced by Kafka consumers in `infrastructure/messaging/consumers/`; and the `cypher_enabled` feature flag in `services/rag-chat/config.py` that only gated the eval-only `RetrievalPlanBuilder.use_cypher` after PLAN-0067 moved the main path to LLM tool-use. Detection heuristic: for every application-layer class with a name suggesting a pipeline step (`*Enricher`, `*Builder`, `*Classifier`, `*Pipeline`, `*Assembler`, `*Scorer`), run `grep -rn ClassName services/ apps/ \| grep -v "/tests/\|test_\|__init__\|.mypy_cache"`. If all non-test references are (a) the definition, (b) DI construction in `app.py`, (c) a docstring in another module — but no call site is reachable from a registered API route, Kafka consumer, or scheduled job — the class is a candidate orphan. Prevention: when an upstream entry-point method is deleted or refactored, immediately grep for callers of every collaborator the deleted method used to invoke; if zero non-test callers remain, prune the collaborator in the same PR. Status: FIXED for known instances (2026-05-24 orphan sweep). Reference: `docs/audits/2026-05-24-investigation-graphenricher-dormant.md`, PLAN-0067 W11-3. Related: HR-065 (counter without UPDATE), HR-064 (LLM hallucination guard). | Architecture, Testing | all |

| BP-538 | Code comment claiming "TanStack won't retry 4xx" on a mutation is incorrect — TanStack's default 4xx guard is a `useQuery`-only behavior. A comment was written in `lib/api/intelligence.ts` saying "retries won't fire on 4xx (TanStack default)" next to `retry: 3` on a `useMutation`. | BP-535 | TypeScript `number` type for backend `float | None` field causes silent arithmetic errors — when a Python backend declares a field as `float | None = None`, the TypeScript frontend type must be `number | null`, not `number`. In JavaScript, arithmetic on `null` produces `0` (not `NaN`), so `null - null === 0` instead of `NaN`. This means a chart rendering `(pt.positive_ratio ?? 0) - (pt.negative_ratio ?? 0)` for a day where the backend returned `null` will plot `0` (a misleading flat line) instead of a gap. The Vitest unit tests also pass incorrect data if the fixture omits null cases — the type mismatch is invisible until live data exercises the null branch. Fix: (1) update all TypeScript interfaces to `number | null` for any field that is `Optional[float]` / `float | None` in the Pydantic model; (2) use `?? NaN` (not `?? 0`) in arithmetic operations — `NaN` causes lightweight-charts to render a gap instead of a misleading zero. Prevention: when adding a TypeScript type for a new API response, cross-check every numeric field in the Pydantic schema for nullability; prefer `?? NaN` over `?? 0` in chart arithmetic to distinguish "no data" from "the value is exactly 0". Status: FIXED (2026-05-22; G-004). Reference: `apps/worldview-web/types/api.ts:SentimentTimeseriesPoint`, `apps/worldview-web/components/instrument/quote/TAOverlayPanel.tsx:273`. | Frontend, TypeScript | apps/worldview-web |
| BP-536 | KG `OutboxRepository.append()` is non-idempotent — unlike the NLP pipeline outbox which accepts a caller-supplied deterministic `event_id` + executes `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (event_id) DO NOTHING`, the knowledge-graph `OutboxRepository.append()` generates a new `uuid4()` on every call and has no conflict guard. If a consumer crashes after the outbox row is written but before the dispatcher publishes it, replaying the triggering Kafka message causes a second `append()` call → a second outbox row → a second downstream Kafka publish → duplicate entity-dirty events → redundant S7 re-enrichment cycles and potential double-counting in aggregate workers. Fix: (1) add an `event_id: UUID` parameter to `append()` — callers supply a deterministic ID derived from the triggering event (e.g. `uuid5(namespace, f"{entity_id}:{event_type}:{epoch_bucket}")`); (2) change the INSERT SQL to `ON CONFLICT (event_id) DO NOTHING`; (3) add a `UNIQUE` constraint on `outbox.event_id` if not already present. Prevention: every outbox `append()` call site MUST supply a stable, content-derived `event_id` so that consumer replay is idempotent end-to-end. Status: OPEN (2026-05-22; G-006/G-007). Reference: `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/infrastructure/outbox/outbox_repository.py`. | Distributed, Knowledge Graph | knowledge-graph |
| BP-545 | `getTopNews()` sends no auth token → hits strict 20 req/min unauthenticated IP bucket → 429 on dashboard. | BP-527 | `dict(request.query_params)` forwarding bypasses FastAPI typed validation — passing raw query params via `raw_params = dict(request.query_params)` to downstream services skips all type checking, range enforcement, and length limits at the gateway layer. A caller can supply `min_confidence=not-a-float`, `min_confidence=99.9`, or `focus_node=<UUID>AAAA...` (37+ chars) and the gateway forwards them unchanged. The downstream service may accept, reject, or silently coerce the value. The 422 response the user sees (if any) comes from S7, not S9, with a different error format and no rate-limit accounting at the gateway. Fix: declare each forwarded parameter as a typed FastAPI `Query()` parameter with constraints (`ge=`, `le=`, `max_length=`); build the downstream param dict from the typed values; remove `raw_params` forwarding entirely. Before: `if "min_confidence" in raw_params: s7_params["min_confidence"] = raw_params["min_confidence"]`. After: `min_confidence: float | None = Query(default=None, ge=0.0, le=1.0)` then `if min_confidence is not None: s7_params["min_confidence"] = str(min_confidence)`. The 422 response is generated at the gateway (S9), never reaches S7, and is consistently formatted. Prevention: every proxy endpoint that forwards query params to a downstream service MUST declare those params as typed `Query()` annotations — never use `request.query_params` dict for forwarded params. Status: FIXED (2026-05-22; F-SEC-001/F-SEC-002). Reference: `services/api-gateway/src/api_gateway/routes/intelligence.py:get_entity_intelligence`, `services/api-gateway/src/api_gateway/routes/intelligence.py:get_entity_graph`. | Security, API Design | api-gateway |
| BP-551 | LLM tool-result follow-up must use OpenAI spec — `role: "tool"` + `tool_call_id` (BLOCKING). | BP-552 | Middleware-set `ContextVar` does NOT reliably propagate into route handlers that spawn nested async tasks. A FastAPI middleware that calls `set_current_jwt(token)` in its post-validate hook works for routes that consume the ContextVar synchronously in the same task — but a route that schedules tool execution via `asyncio.create_task` / `gather` / a long-running orchestrator loop may see an empty ContextVar inside those nested tasks (Python copies the context at task creation; subsequent middleware mutations are not visible). Symptom: tool handlers' downstream HTTP clients send no `X-Internal-JWT` header → KG/S7 returns 401 → handlers silent-degrade to `[]` → orchestrator emits `all_tools_failed` with no usable error trace. | BP-554 | "Tool returned empty" and "tool errored" must be distinct orchestrator paths. | BP-555 | Generic `except Exception as e: log(type(e).__name__)` hides the actual error and crushes debug time. | BP-559 | Completion-cache key must bump on prompt change — cached responses can hide upstream regressions for weeks. | BP-572 | Classifier latency shadowed cache-hit fast path — re-classifying on every read is defensive duplication. PLAN-0095 W2 T-W2-03: `_execute_streaming_inner` ran `validate_input()` (Layer 2 LLM injection classifier, 5-8 s on DeepInfra) BEFORE `check_cache()`, so the ~15% cache-hit traffic still paid the classifier cost. Cached completions were already classifier-validated on their first write (writer flow: `validate_input → check_cache miss → classifier → cache.set`), so a poisoned message cannot enter the cache unless it already passed the classifier once. Detection: any pipeline step with latency >100 ms placed BEFORE a cache lookup is a code smell — read every `pipeline.validate_*`/`pipeline.classify_*`/`pipeline.score_*` ordering against the cache check and challenge "does the cache write path provably guarantee this invariant already holds?". If yes, move the slow step AFTER the cache. Fix: swap the two `await` calls in the orchestrator + add a regression test `test_chat_pipeline_cache_hit_skips_classifier` that mocks `check_cache → hit` and asserts `validate_input.assert_not_called()`. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0095 W2 T-W2-03, 2026-05-26). | BP-574 | AGE schema cache leaks across SQLAlchemy session — bootstrap-then-MERGE on the same connection silently no-ops. PLAN-0096 W3 T-W3-01 (2026-05-26): `AgeSyncWorker._bootstrap_age_labels` created the `TemporalEvent` vlabel, committed, then immediately ran phase MERGE statements on the **same** `AsyncSession`. PostgreSQL's plpgsql engine (which backs `ag_catalog.cypher()`) caches the label catalog on each physical connection at first lookup; the post-commit phase MERGE saw the pre-bootstrap snapshot and silently dropped every row — leaving 0 of 14,822 TemporalEvent vertices in AGE despite the worker logging `age_sync_labels_bootstrapped` + `age_sync_temporal_events_complete` happily. Detection: any AGE worker that issues DDL (`create_vlabel`/`create_elabel`) and then a DML (`MERGE`/`MATCH`) on the same session is at risk — the symptom is a silently undercounted vertex/edge label with no exception in the logs. Fix: after the bootstrap `await session.commit()`, call `await session.connection()` then `await connection.invalidate()` so SQLAlchemy drops the physical connection back to the pool; the next `_setup_age_session` checks out a fresh connection and reloads AGE on it. Make the invalidate best-effort (try/except + warning log) so a pool hiccup doesn't crash the cycle. Reconciliation script for any existing backlog: `scripts/reconcile_age_temporal_events.py` (idempotent, `--dry-run` supported). Status: FIXED (PLAN-0096 W3 T-W3-01, 2026-05-26). | BP-571 | `createGateway(accessToken)` inside `useMemo` bypasses canonical `useApiClient()` hook. PRD-0089 Wave G QA (2026-05-26): dozens of new TanStack Query components in `apps/worldview-web/` grabbed `accessToken` from `useAuth()` and constructed `useMemo(() => createGateway(accessToken), [accessToken])` instead of calling `useApiClient()` from `lib/api-client.tsx`. Effects: (a) a new gateway client is constructed on every render — defeats request dedup + centralised token-refresh; (b) tests must mock `@/lib/gateway` (low-level constructor) instead of `@/lib/api-client.useApiClient`, causing test/runtime divergence; (c) token refresh propagation is delayed because the gateway instance is captured in `useMemo([accessToken])` and only swaps when the token rotates. Root cause: the repo has TWO gateway construction paths — `useApiClient()` (canonical, React hook) and `createGateway(accessToken)` (low-level constructor for non-React contexts). New code copies the older `useMemo(createGateway)` pattern from pre-hook components. The hook is the contract; the constructor is an implementation detail. Detection: `git grep -l "createGateway(" apps/worldview-web/{features,components,app,hooks}` should return ONLY `lib/api-client.tsx`. Fix: replace `createGateway(accessToken)` inside any React component with `useApiClient()`, drop the `accessToken` import + `useMemo` wrapper, and update tests to mock `@/lib/api-client.useApiClient` (not `@/lib/gateway`). | BP-581 | Adding an index does not change the query plan until `ANALYZE` refreshes `pg_statistic` — composite-index migrations must ship a paired `ANALYZE`. PLAN-0097 W3 T-W3-01 (2026-05-27): migration 019 created composite `(instrument_id, period_end_date)` indexes on 18 fundamentals tables expecting a 30-100x speedup on the dominant `WHERE instrument_id = :iid ORDER BY period_end_date` query pattern. Until ANALYZE runs, the new composite is invisible to the planner, so the migration's intended speedup is silently deferred to whenever the next autovacuum cycle happens to run. Fix: migration 022 issues `ANALYZE <table>` for each of the 18 tables, wrapped in `op.get_context().autocommit_block()` because ANALYZE cannot execute inside a transaction (sibling family to CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY per BP-393). | BP-582 | Per-item batch endpoints must classify exceptions into a typed reason vocabulary — raw `str(exc)` in the response body is both an info leak and a prompt-injection foothold. PLAN-0097 W3 T-W3-04 (2026-05-27): `POST /v1/fundamentals/batch` previously returned `reason=str(exc)` for per-ticker failures, leaking asyncpg internals, file paths, and (for a maliciously-named ticker) attacker-controlled steering strings into the LLM's tool-result context window. Worse, the LLM cannot reliably retry on `reason="..."` free-form text — it needs a stable signal to decide "skip this ticker forever" vs "transient, try again". Fix: classify exceptions into four typed codes — `invalid_ticker` (InstrumentNotFoundError), `upstream_timeout` (asyncio/built-in TimeoutError), `upstream_404` (status_code==404), `upstream_error` (default bucket) — and route the full exception detail to structlog (server-side only). Defence-in-depth test scans the entire response body text for a sentinel substring placed inside the raised exception message and asserts it never leaks. Prevention: any new per-item batch endpoint whose `reason`/`error` field is read by an LLM tool result MUST (1) map exceptions to a closed vocabulary, (2) log the full exception via structlog only, (3) include a sentinel-leak regression test. | BP-579 | LLM safety classifier intermittently labels benign relationship/graph-discovery queries between named entities as PROMPT_INJECTION even at temperature=0.0. PLAN-0097 W2 T-W2-01 (2026-05-27): the 2026-05-27 chat-eval Phase D produced 2 of 5 INPUT_REJECTED verdicts on Q8 ('How is OpenAI connected to Microsoft? Show me the relationship paths.') across the same prompt — the DeepInfra Meta-Llama-3.1-8B-Instruct-Turbo classifier non-deterministically matched 'show me the relationship paths' against the vague PROMPT_INJECTION category ('smuggle hidden instructions'). The system prompt had no explicit SAFE exemplar for relationship discovery between named entities, so the model defaulted to UNSAFE on ambiguous phrasings. Detection: any new chat-eval question that exercises the knowledge-graph product surface ('how is X connected to Y', 'what is the relationship between A and B', supply-chain, partnerships) is at risk; greplog for 'rag_injection_blocked_layer2' counter spikes on relationship-shape questions. Fix: add an explicit SAFE bullet to the classifier system prompt enumerating the relationship/graph shape (PLAN-0097 W2 T-W2-01, additive only — does not weaken UNSAFE rules); pair with a 13+ benign-query parametrised regression suite that asserts SAFE under a mocked-LLM stub AND under the live DeepInfra classifier (live gated by INTEGRATION_TEST=1 + API key). Bump CLASSIFIER_PROMPT_VERSION constant so downstream classifier-result caches (P2 W4 T-W4-02) invalidate. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0097 W2 T-W2-01, 2026-05-27). Reference: `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/security/llm_injection_classifier.py`, `services/rag-chat/tests/unit/security/test_llm_injection_classifier_benign_relationships.py`, `docs/audits/2026-05-27-plan-0097-classifier-grader-investigation.md`. | ML & LLM, Security | rag-chat |
| BP-583 | R40 sentinel-tenant visibility filter applied at only one of N parallel SQL surfaces — partial fix re-armed the inverse-visibility bug at every untouched site. PLAN-0098 follow-up to PLAN-0097 Phase-D code review §2.3 (2026-05-27): PLAN-0097 W4 T-W4-01 (commit `8c3a9249`) added the `PUBLIC_TENANT_ID` (`00000000-...`) OR-leg to `news_query._ENTITY_ARTICLES_SQL` but missed the four structurally-identical OR-clauses in `chunk_search.py` (`_search_chunks` line 172, `_search_sections` line 261, the section-COUNT branch line 312, and `lexical_search` line 426). | BP-586 | PUBLIC_TENANT_ID sentinel substitution applied in the consumer envelope but per-mention tenant stamp guarded by a redundant `if tenant_id is not None`, leaving the door open for any downstream block (entity resolution, deep extraction, novelty backfill) to leak a mention with `tenant_id=None` past the stamp and into the `entity_mentions` INSERT — the NOT NULL constraint (migration 0020) fails the INSERT, exception treated as retryable, consumer loops forever, table stays at 0 rows. | BP-587 | BuildKit gRPC frontend collapses under ≥25–30 concurrent build targets — `docker compose up -d --build --force-recreate <N services>` aborts with `target <X>: failed to solve: frontend grpc server closed unexpectedly`, where the failing target name varies between runs (load-induced, not Dockerfile-specific). PLAN-0089 Wave K rebuild investigation (2026-05-26): a single sweeping rebuild of all microservices saturated the BuildKit gRPC frontend; the same compose file rebuilt cleanly when split into 4–10-service batches. Symptom: the same gRPC error appearing twice in a row on *different* targets is the load-induced signature (distinct from a real Dockerfile fault, which fails the same target every time). Detection: if a repeated `docker compose build` lists a different failing target each run, treat as overload. Fix: batch builds by service family (e.g. portfolio + portfolio-consumer + portfolio-migrate together; nlp-pipeline + its consumers/workers together) with 4–10 targets per batch. Prevention: any "rebuild everything" runbook step MUST script the batch split — do not pass 25+ targets to a single `docker compose build` invocation. Status: KNOWN-WORKAROUND (PLAN-0089 Wave K, 2026-05-26). Reference: Wave K rebuild investigation notes. | Build & CI, Operational | infra/compose |
| BP-588 | `docker compose` sibling services that each declare their own `build:` block produce N distinct images even though they ship the same code — rebuilding the "family leader" leaves siblings stale. PLAN-0089 Wave K rebuild investigation (2026-05-26): every `*-consumer`, `*-dispatcher`, `*-migrate`, `*-scheduler`, `*-worker` in `infra/compose/docker-compose.yml` has its own `build:` block, so compose treats them as `worldview-<service>:latest`, `worldview-<service>-migrate:latest`, … and a rebuild of one image never propagates to the others. Symptom: "I built family-leader X but X-migrate is still running old code". Detection: `docker images | grep worldview-<family>` shows multiple tags with different creation timestamps after what was meant to be a single family rebuild. Fix (proper): refactor sibling entries to `image: worldview-<family>:latest` referencing the leader's `build:` output (no `build:` block on siblings). Fix (workaround): always build every sibling explicitly — never assume one build covers a family. Prevention: a compose lint/test that asserts at most one `build:` block per service-family prefix, and a runbook line telling operators to enumerate sibling services in any rebuild command. Status: KNOWN-WORKAROUND (PLAN-0089 Wave K, 2026-05-26). Reference: `infra/compose/docker-compose.yml` (every `*-consumer`/`*-migrate`/`*-worker` block). | Build & CI, Infrastructure | infra/compose |
| BP-589 | BuildKit's content-hash layer cache occasionally returns a stale layer despite a tracked source change — the new file is absent from the built image even though `git ls-files` confirms it is tracked and `.dockerignore` does not exclude it. PLAN-0089 Wave K rebuild investigation (2026-05-26): suspected interaction between a whitelist-style `.dockerignore` and many sibling builds racing on the same daemon (see BP-587/BP-588). Symptom: `docker run <image> ls <expected-path>` does not list a file that was just added in the working tree and committed. Detection: any "I added file X but the container can't find it" issue where the file is present in `git ls-files` and not in `.dockerignore`. | BP-590 | Multiple Claude Code sessions sharing the same Git worktree silently corrupt each other — observed in PLAN-0089 Wave K (2026-05-26): branch silently switched 3 times mid-session; one session's `git reset HEAD~1` orphaned another session's commit (recovered via reflog, with T-08 and T-09 collapsing into a single later commit); `git stash pop` injected conflict markers into 4 backend files an agent did not expect; `TRACKING.md` edits returned success but were overwritten seconds later by a sibling session. Detection: commits appearing in `git log` that the current agent did not author; `HEAD` pointing at a different branch than the one the agent started on; spontaneous conflict markers in files that were clean a moment ago; "succeeded" Edit/Write operations whose content is gone on re-read. Fix (proper): every parallel session MUST run inside its own `git worktree add <path> -b <branch>` checkout — there is no shared `.git/index` / working tree, so the corruption surface disappears. Fix (workaround): one worktree = one agent; if sharing is unavoidable, use a sentinel file (e.g. `.git/CLAUDE_AGENT_LOCK`) to serialise destructive ops, and prefer `git commit` over `git stash` so nothing depends on an unnamed stash entry. Prevention: orchestrators that spawn parallel agents MUST allocate a fresh worktree per child; CLAUDE.md guidance updated alongside this entry. Status: KNOWN-WORKAROUND (PLAN-0089 Wave K, 2026-05-26). Reference: Wave K rebuild investigation notes; `CLAUDE.md` "Parallel Sessions" subsection; RULES.md R42. | Operational, Process | repo-wide |

| BP-592 | Batch endpoint iterator desync on partial-failure tickers — `fetch_iter = iter(fetch_results)` + `next(fetch_iter)` advanced only when `task is not None`, but `fetch_results` only contained the *pending* (non-None) gather outcomes. The result-assembly loop iterated over the FULL `fetch_tasks` list (including ticker slots with `task=None` from resolution failures). The moment a `task is None` branch fired its `continue`, the iterator cursor and the loop index drifted — every subsequent ticker received the previous ticker's outcome. PLAN-0099 W1 T-W1-01 (2026-05-27): symptom surfaced in chat-eval Q4 (`tests/validation/chat_eval/runs/20260527T154018Z/agg_q4.json`) where NVDA Q3 FY2025 reported AMD's $10.3B value. Detection: any batch endpoint that mixes per-item resolve+fetch phases and uses an iterator pulled from a *filtered* gather result list while looping over the *unfiltered* input list is at risk; grep for `iter(.*results)` paired with `next(.*iter)` inside a loop with `continue` branches. Fix: bind each gather outcome to its originating key BEFORE the assembly loop — `dict(zip(pending_keys, gather_results, strict=True))` — then index by key in the loop, never by iterator position. The `strict=True` zip surfaces any future length asymmetry immediately. Prevention: any per-item batch endpoint MUST bind fan-out outcomes structurally (by ticker / id / key), not positionally. Regression tests: `test_fundamentals_batch_mixed_resolution_outcomes` (valid + invalid-resolution + valid; asserts ticker[2]'s revenue ≠ ticker[0]'s revenue) + `test_fundamentals_batch_first_ticker_fetch_timeout_does_not_bleed_into_second` (TimeoutError on ticker[0]; asserts ticker[1] receives its own data). | BP-607 | Chat-eval TTFT-p95 silently overcounts on tool-using questions because the harness counts only content tokens, but tool-use questions emit metadata + `tool_call` + `tool_result` for tens of seconds before the first synthesised token. | BP-606 | `news_query.get_entity_articles` returns zero articles for tickers whose entity linkage lives ONLY in the denormalised `chunks.entity_mentions` JSONB column (not in the normalised `entity_mentions` table), even when the chunk text clearly mentions the entity. PLAN-0100 W1 (2026-05-27, Q2 MSTR canary): MSTR's `019e0db6-2e39-7e04-aaf8-9ec675797470` had 8 chunks with JSONB `entity_id=MSTR` but ZERO rows in the normalised table — the entity-article SQL joined only the table and returned empty, making MSTR (and any other low-coverage ticker: small-caps, recent IPOs, non-US tickers) invisible to chat retrieval. The empty result triggered the BP-604 fallback-drift hallucination. Detection: any ticker where `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM entity_mentions WHERE resolved_entity_id=<uuid>` is zero AND `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM chunks WHERE entity_mentions @> jsonb_build_array(jsonb_build_object('entity_id', '<uuid>'))` is non-zero. Fix: extend `_ENTITY_ARTICLES_SQL` so the `entity_article_ids` CTE UNIONs (a) the original `entity_mentions` table SELECT and (b) a denormalised `chunks.entity_mentions @> jsonb_build_array(jsonb_build_object('entity_id', CAST(:entity_id AS TEXT)))` SELECT. Both legs honour the R35 three-row-class tenant filter (NULL + tenant + PUBLIC_TENANT_ID sentinel). The GIN index on `chunks.entity_mentions` accelerates Leg-2. Companion: `scripts/backfill_entity_mentions_from_chunks_jsonb.py` is the idempotent write-side closer (belt-and-braces, not required for read-path correctness). Prevention: any future denormalised/normalised dual-write pair MUST have its read-side aggregator UNION both sources OR a CI fixture asserting parity; lineage gaps are detected post-facto only by chat-eval verdicts. Regression test: `services/nlp-pipeline/tests/unit/infrastructure/test_news_query_jsonb_fallback.py::TestEntityArticlesJsonbFallback` (5 cases: both legs present, UNIONed, JSONB containment syntax, tenant filter on JSONB leg, shared `:entity_id` parameter). Status: FIXED (PLAN-0100 W1 T-W1-01, 2026-05-27). Reference: `services/nlp-pipeline/src/nlp_pipeline/infrastructure/nlp_db/repositories/news_query.py`, `docs/audits/2026-05-27-plan-0100-q2-mstr-entity-drift-deepdive.md` §2. | Data Lineage, RAG & Tool Use | nlp-pipeline |
| BP-580 | Chat-eval grader exact-string tool-name match penalises the model for choosing the (correct) batch-tool variant. PLAN-0097 W2 T-W2-03 (2026-05-27): the 2026-05-27 chat-eval recorded Q4 v1/v6 verdicts as MARGINAL because ground truth asserted `required_tools_any_of=["get_fundamentals_history"]` while the model — following PLAN-0095 W2 + PLAN-0097 W3 intent-map guidance for multi-ticker questions — invoked `get_fundamentals_history_batch`. Same family: `traverse_graph` vs `get_entity_paths` (KG traversal aliases). The grader's substring check `any(t in required_tools for t in tools_called)` had no equivalence layer, so semantically-identical tool calls failed the assertion. Detection: any time a batch/parallelized variant of an existing tool ships, audit `tests/validation/chat_eval/grading.py::_TOOL_EQUIVALENTS` for the singular ↔ batch mapping; missing entries cause spurious MARGINAL verdicts. Fix: `_TOOL_EQUIVALENTS: dict[str, set[str]]` mapping with symmetric entries + `_tool_requirement_satisfied()` helper that intersects `called_set` with the equivalence set per requirement. Companion changes: (a) when `error.code == 'INPUT_REJECTED'` the missing-tool reason is suppressed (the upstream classifier rejected before the model could choose any tool — the request never reached tool selection); (b) refusal-vs-USELESS policy made explicit in the module docstring (SHORT + uncited → USELESS; LONG OR citing + refusal token → honest data-gap, NOT a refusal). | BP-612 | Chat-eval grader honest-quote exemption window too narrow → NVDA-near-AMD false positive on PLAN-0101 Q4-variant grading. The grader detects honest data-gap refusals via marker phrases ("do not appear in the retrieved results for AMD", "I cannot find", etc.) within a ±N-char window of the disputed numeric claim; the legacy window (±60 chars, singular `"do not appear"` only) missed plural refusal phrasing ("NVIDIA and AMD do not appear") AND refusals sitting ~95 chars after the offending number, classifying honest refusals as HARMFUL fabrications. PLAN-0101 W3 (2026-05-28): Q4 v3 (NVDA fundamentals) flagged HARMFUL because the answer correctly said "NVIDIA's Q1 FY2026 revenue figures do not appear in the retrieved results for AMD" but the marker landed ~95 chars after the AMD revenue-cap test value, outside the ±60 window; the verdict pipeline therefore counted it as fabrication. Detection: any grader-flagged HARMFUL on a question whose answer explicitly names "do not appear", "I cannot find", "no data" within the same paragraph as the disputed value; verify by re-running with a wider window. Fix: expand the marker set to include plural forms ("do not appear", "are not present", "could not be located") and widen the honest-quote exemption window to **±150 chars** in `tests/validation/chat_eval/grading.py` around the revenue-cap branch. Prevention: every new refusal-style training of the model MUST be paired with a grader-marker audit; the marker set lives next to the honest-refusal policy docstring in `grading.py` so future tweaks are co-located. Regression test: `tests/validation/chat_eval/test_grading.py::TestGraderHonestRefusalExemption` covers ±150 char placement at boundaries 0 / 95 / 149 / 151 and plural-marker matching. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0101 W3, 2026-05-28). Reference: `tests/validation/chat_eval/grading.py:581-706`, commit `91a363a0`. | Testing, Eval Design | tests/validation/chat_eval |
| BP-613 | Chat-eval harness `ChatRunResult.final_answer` is empty when the SSE stream emits only `delta`/`token` chunks and the terminal `done` event omits an aggregate `final_answer` payload (or carries it truncated by mid-stream cancellation). The legacy assembly path took `done.data.final_answer` verbatim; when missing, the harness recorded `final_answer=""` and the grader scored the question USELESS even though the streamed tokens contained a complete, well-formed answer. PLAN-0101 W3 (2026-05-28): observed on multiple chat-eval runs where the backend cleanly streamed an answer but the orchestrator's `emit_done` body lacked `final_answer` (the streaming-direct branch shipped by PLAN-0099 W1 SSE chunk streaming — BP-595 — emits only `delta` frames and writes nothing to `done.data.final_answer`). Detection: any chat-eval row whose `output_tokens > 0` AND `final_answer == ""`; cross-check `event_timings.token_count` against `final_answer` length. Fix: harness `_events_to_result()` now reassembles a `joined_tokens` fallback by concatenating every `delta`/`token` event payload in order; the result chooses `final_answer` when present AND non-empty, otherwise falls back to `joined_tokens`. The fallback also strips any trailing `[N#]` citation marker whose index exceeds the citations actually emitted (defence-in-depth — see BP-616 reservation in PLAN-0102 W5 for the longer-wins ↔ numeric-grounding hardening). Prevention: any new SSE event kind that carries user-visible text MUST be added to the `_TOKEN_EVENT_KINDS` constant in `harness.py`; a unit test asserts the constant matches the orchestrator's emitter set. Regression tests (4 in `tests/validation/chat_eval/test_harness_latency.py::TestBP613AnswerAssemblyFallback`): `final_answer` empty + tokens present → fallback used; `final_answer` missing key + tokens present → fallback used; `final_answer` present and non-empty → fallback ignored; `joined_tokens` and `final_answer` both empty → result empty (graceful). Status: FIXED (PLAN-0101 W3, 2026-05-28). Reference: `tests/validation/chat_eval/harness.py` (`_events_to_result` + `_TOKEN_EVENT_KINDS`), `tests/validation/chat_eval/test_harness_latency.py:106` (`TestBP613AnswerAssemblyFallback`), commit `91a363a0`. | Testing, Eval Design | tests/validation/chat_eval |

| BP-617 | Large-universe Kafka payloads silently dead-lettered when a per-message processing watchdog (`messaging.kafka.consumer.base.ConsumerConfig.message_processing_timeout_s`) is set below the realistic 99th-percentile processing time of the dominant payload shape. | BP-610 | SQLAlchemy Core `update()` statement executed against an async session is buffered, NOT flushed — when a later op in the same UoW raises an exception that is caught-and-swallowed (try/except) the buffered UPDATE is lost on the next commit even though every section-write in the same UoW persists. PLAN-0101 (2026-05-28): `instruments.last_fundamentals_ingest_at` stayed NULL for ALL 629 instruments despite `FundamentalsConsumer.process_message` correctly awaiting `uow.instruments.touch_fundamentals_ingest_at(instrument_id, ingested_at)` at line 589 — section rows AND `instrument_fundamentals_snapshot` rows landed every cycle (logs showed `materialized` + `snapshot_upserted`), but the touch UPDATE silently dropped on the floor. The audit confirmed (a) migration 021 applied, (b) PG triggers absent, (c) no `failed_tasks`/dead-letter rows, (d) `instruments.updated_at` ran BEFORE the materialized log → the touch UPDATE never reached the database. Root cause was a Docker-image staleness compounded by the absence of a defensive flush; the running container's `/app/.venv/.../fundamentals_consumer.py` had zero references to `touch_fundamentals_ingest_at` (predated commit 8450666b). Fix: put an explicit `await self._session.flush()` INSIDE the repository method, matching the repo-wide convention (`content-store`, `alert`, `rag-chat`, `content-ingestion` all flush inside repo writes); this ensures the UPDATE reaches the transaction before any consumer-level try/except can mask a later failure. Detection: any "observational" column written by a single repo call wrapped in the same UoW as a best-effort try/except block; cross-check by joining the column against the operation log timestamp — if the column is NULL on rows that successfully ran the surrounding writes, the buffer-and-drop pattern is in play. Prevention: every repo write method that targets a tracking/freshness column MUST end in `await self._session.flush()` so callers cannot forget; never rely on the consumer-layer commit boundary alone when the same UoW contains a try/except that swallows downstream exceptions. Regression test: `services/market-data/tests/integration/test_repositories.py::TestPgInstrumentRepository::test_touch_fundamentals_ingest_at_persists`. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0101, 2026-05-28). Reference: `services/market-data/src/market_data/infrastructure/db/repositories/instrument_repo.py::touch_fundamentals_ingest_at`, `docs/audits/2026-05-28-plan-0101-bp-610-touch-at.md`. NOTE: image rebuild required for live activation (`docker compose build market-data && up -d --no-deps --force-recreate market-data-fundamentals-consumer`); rebuild + container recreate performed during fix session, end-to-end refresh verification deferred to QA round (manual trigger requires an internal-JWT-signed POST to market-ingestion). | Data Pipeline, ORM | market-data |
| BP-618 | PhaseTimings double-record risk on `llm_synthesis_streaming` — the chat orchestrator records the second-turn LLM stream wall-clock at TWO sites that are mutually exclusive only by control-flow accident: the streaming-success branch (`chat_orchestrator.py:~1717`) and the streaming-failure except clause (`~1707`) that returns immediately after recording. PhaseTimings.record() accumulates by design — a future refactor that breaks the early-return invariant would silently double-count synthesis ms, halving `tps_streaming` everywhere and triggering false aggregate-gate failures. PLAN-0102 W4 T-W4-02 (2026-05-29): introduced `PhaseTimings.record_once(name, ms)` that (a) raises AssertionError when `PHASE_TIMINGS_STRICT=1` is set (test conftest), (b) WARN-logs `phase_timings_double_record` with prior + new values and falls back to `record` semantics in production (so a metrics-only bug never crashes the user-facing chat stream). Prevention: every phase that is guaranteed-to-fire-at-most-once by control-flow design MUST use `record_once` so the invariant is mechanical, not narrative. | BP-620 | Frontend `/chat` page fired `GET /api/v1/threads/{client-minted-uuid}` BEFORE the backend had ever heard of the thread, returning 404 and flashing a generic error banner the moment the user clicked "New chat" — even before typing a message. Same class of race triggered by `useChatStream.send()`'s first-message thread mint (the hook calls `setActiveThreadId(crypto.randomUUID())` so SSE chunks have a stable id, but rag-chat only persists the thread once the first user message lands). The TanStack Query subscription on `activeThreadId` had `enabled: !!activeThreadId`, with NO guard for "is this id server-known yet" — every fresh client UUID immediately fired `getThread(uuid)` → 404 → error banner. Same shape also affects stale-localStorage thread ids and browser-back navigation into a thread that has since been deleted. PLAN-0102 W7-frontend (2026-05-28): introduced an `ephemeralThreadIdsRef` set in `app/(app)/chat/page.tsx` that holds every client-minted UUID; the per-thread useQuery `enabled` clause is gated on `!ephemeralThreadIdsRef.has(activeThreadId)`; an effect tied to the threads-list refresh promotes the id out of the set as soon as rag-chat confirms its existence (which happens via `refetchThreads()` after the `done` SSE event). Defensive 404 handler in the queryFn converts `GatewayError(status=404)` into an in-memory empty-thread stub instead of surfacing the error banner — covers the stale-id paths the ephemeral gate cannot pre-empt. Detection: any 404 in the gateway access log on `GET /v1/threads/{uuid}` paired with a frontend `Referer: /chat` AND the uuid not appearing in any prior `POST /v1/chat/stream` body — classic "fetched-before-persisted" race. Browser DevTools network panel will show the 404 firing within ~10 ms of clicking "New chat" with zero user input in between. Prevention: every `useQuery` whose key is a client-minted resource id MUST gate `enabled` on "server has acknowledged this id" (either via list presence or an explicit `isPersisted` flag), AND its `queryFn` MUST treat 404 as a benign empty-state rather than letting `GatewayError` propagate to the error boundary. | BP-621 | Chat-eval `tps_streaming` metric reported `None` on ~100% of questions because the orchestrator only recorded an `llm_synthesis_streaming` phase on the SECOND-turn streaming branch (after tool calls). Direct-text answers ("What is Apple?" — LLM responds without calling tools, common case) and FIX-LIVE-Y "tool-then-direct-text" answers (tools fired in iter-0, iter-1 LLM returned direct text and the orchestrator set `_skip_final_stream=True`) both terminated WITHOUT ever entering the second-turn `stream_chat` path. The harness `_compute_tps_streaming` then returned `None` ("no data, skip the gate") on every such question. With ~80%+ of chat-eval questions taking these branches, the streaming-TPS gate had no data and the operator could not distinguish "stream is genuinely slow" from "the metric is structurally absent". PLAN-0102 W4 T-W4-B (2026-05-29): the orchestrator now also records `llm_direct_text_generation` (equal to the THIS iterations `chat_with_tools` wall-clock, the call that produced the user-visible text) on BOTH the iter-0 pure-direct-text branch and the iter>0 FIX-LIVE-Y branch, using `record_once` so a future loop refactor cannot silently double-count. The harness `_compute_tps_streaming` accepts EITHER `llm_synthesis_streaming` OR `llm_direct_text_generation` as the denominator (synthesis-stream wins when both present — defensive). | BP-622 | All rag-chat tool handlers with named-parameter signatures (no `**kwargs`) silently failed when DeepSeek emitted an unknown kwarg: `MarketHandler._handle_screen_universe(market_cap_min=…, …)` accepted 7 known params; LLM passed `revenue_growth_yoy_min: 0.0` (a valid metric per `market-data/.../metric_extractor.py:171`); Python raised `TypeError: _handle_screen_universe() got an unexpected keyword argument 'revenue_growth_yoy_min'`; outer `ToolExecutor.execute` swallowed it as `tool_argument_error` and returned `None` → 41 ms tool call, 0 items returned, LLM wrote 'no data found'. Same anti-pattern shape as F-LIVE-Q (silent prompt-input drop). PLAN-0103 W1 (2026-05-29): centralised the fix in `handlers/base.py` via `filter_kwargs_to_signature(target, tool_name, args)` — introspects the handler signature once, splits LLM args into `(known, unknown)`, emits `tool_unknown_kwarg` structlog event + increments `rag_chat_tool_unknown_kwarg_total{tool_name, kwarg}` Prom counter per unknown key, then calls `target(**known)`. All 6 handlers' `execute()` updated to use a `dispatch` dict + the filter. Screener also got `revenue_growth_yoy_min/max`, `gross_margin_min/max`, `roe_min`, `dividend_yield_min/max` parameters wired through to `ScreenFilterRequest` entries against the matching market-data metric column. Detection: any sustained `rag_chat_tool_unknown_kwarg_total` rate above 0 for a single (tool, kwarg) pair → either teach the handler the new parameter (preferred when the kwarg is a real metric) or tighten the tool description so the LLM stops asking. Cross-check: `tool_argument_error` events in rag-chat logs are now structurally impossible from this class of mismatch (filter strips before dispatch). Prevention: when adding a new `_handle_*` method to ANY handler, register it in the handler's `dispatch` dict — never re-introduce a `_handle_X(**args)` branch that bypasses the filter.
