| BP-623 | All rag-chat upstream client paths collapsed transport-layer failures (DNS / connect refused / timeout / HTTP 5xx) and legitimate empty results (HTTP 200 with empty payload) into the same return shape: `BaseUpstreamClient._get/_post` returned `{}` on every error class; per-tool handlers then mapped that to `[]`; `ToolExecutor.execute` returned `[]`; the orchestrator's three-state classifier labelled the call `status="empty"` (item not None, count=0); the LLM was given `(no matching rows returned)` plus an entity-anchored "no data for THIS entity" guidance message — and answered "No data was found" even when the upstream was DOWN. Real-user audit `docs/audits/2026-05-29-plan-0103-real-user-failures.md` Q4/Q5 root cause: `worldview-market-data-1` was down, `get_fundamentals_history_batch` returned `{}` in 16 ms, the LLM had no way to distinguish a transport failure from a legitimate empty result. PLAN-0103 W2 (2026-05-29): introduced `UpstreamTransportError(BaseException)` (NOT Exception — so per-handler `except Exception: return []` guards do NOT swallow it) in `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/infrastructure/clients/base.py`; modified `_get`/`_post` to RAISE for ConnectError / ConnectTimeout / RemoteProtocolError / TimeoutException / HTTP 5xx (with `reason` ∈ `{upstream_unreachable, upstream_timeout, upstream_5xx}`, `status_code`, `elapsed_ms`, `path`); HTTP 4xx still returns `{}` (a client-side problem, not an outage — promoting 4xx would over-trigger the user-facing outage copy on every legitimate not-found). Added `TransportErrorMarker` dataclass sentinel (`services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/pipeline/transport_error.py`) + matching `except UpstreamTransportError` branch in `ToolExecutor.execute` that returns the marker instead of `None`. Orchestrator (`chat_orchestrator.py`) detects the marker in the tool-items interpretation loop and (1) emits SSE `tool_result` with `status="transport_error"` + `reason` + `status_code` + `elapsed_ms` (new optional fields on `SSEEmitter.emit_tool_result`); (2) injects a structured `role="tool"` content `(transport_error: <reason> status_code=<sc> elapsed_ms=<ms>)` instead of the misleading `(no matching rows returned)`; (3) injects a user-guidance message telling the LLM "the data source is temporarily unreachable — suggest they retry, do NOT say 'no data was found', do NOT substitute facts from training data". System prompt `libs/prompts/src/prompts/chat/tool_use.py` v1.2 adds the symmetric LLM-side rule: "When a tool_result has status=transport_error, DO NOT say 'no data was found'. Say 'I cannot reach the <upstream> data source right now — please retry'." Detection: any SSE stream with `tool_result.status="transport_error"` paired with an answer body containing "no data was found" / "did not return any" → orchestrator wiring regressed. Cross-check: structured-log search for `tool_transport_error` + the call's `reason` field. Prevention: NEVER catch httpx exceptions in upstream clients and return `{}` — let `BaseUpstreamClient` raise so the executor can classify centrally. `UpstreamTransportError` MUST inherit from `BaseException` (pinned by `test_upstream_transport_error_inherits_from_baseexception_not_exception`); any future rewrite that demotes it to `Exception` re-introduces the swallowing pattern. Regression tests (13 in two files): `services/rag-chat/tests/unit/infrastructure/clients/test_transport_error_disambiguation.py` (7 tests: BaseException inheritance, connect → unreachable, timeout → timeout, 5xx → 5xx with status_code, 4xx → {}, 422 → {}, 200-empty → {}, 200-empty-list → passthrough) + `services/rag-chat/tests/unit/application/pipeline/test_transport_error_propagation.py` (6 tests: executor catches & returns marker, marker preserves 5xx status, SSE emitter renders transport_error payload, SSE shape unchanged for ok/empty statuses). Also updated 5 legacy tests in `test_clients.py` + `test_s3_client_temporal.py` that pinned the old `return []` behaviour. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W2, 2026-05-29). Reference: `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/infrastructure/clients/base.py::UpstreamTransportError`, `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/pipeline/transport_error.py::TransportErrorMarker`, `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/pipeline/tool_executor.py::ToolExecutor.execute` (transport-error branch), `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/use_cases/chat_orchestrator.py` (`_transport_errors_by_call_id` dict + SSE emit + role="tool" injection + user-guidance branch), `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/pipeline/sse_emitter.py::SSEEmitter.emit_tool_result` (new optional fields), `libs/prompts/src/prompts/chat/tool_use.py` v1.2. | Upstream Integration, Tool Dispatch, LLM Integration | rag-chat |
| BP-624 | Morning brief v4.1 prompt rendered only 4 of 6 named sections in the wild — Risks + Opportunities and Bonus context were silently dropped, leaving the brief with a truncated structure that the user (and the operator) had no observability into. Root cause was prompt permissiveness: the v4.1 spec listed all 6 sections but used "expected" / "output sections in this order" language, NOT "MANDATORY"; on quiet news days the LLM took the path of least resistance and skipped the last two whole categories. Compounding issue (product ask): the dashboard collapsed `MorningBriefCard` view rendered the first 3 lines of `narrative` (clamp-3) instead of a purpose-built summary paragraph, so the user landed on a brief that started mid-section. Added `BriefParser.split_summary_paragraph()` (extracts the paragraph + strips `[N#]` markers + soft-caps at 300 chars via sentence boundary) and `BriefParser.check_section_completeness()` (returns missing section names from the `V42_EXPECTED_SECTIONS` tuple). Frontend `MorningBriefCard` collapsed view now reads `summary_paragraph ▸ summary ▸ narrative head` fallback chain. Edge case caught during impl: the case-insensitive `split_summary_paragraph` also matches legacy v2.2 `## SUMMARY` headings — the use case must only override `narrative` with the post-Summary remainder when the v2.2 splitter did NOT also produce a `summary` (otherwise the `## DETAILS` header re-appears in the expanded view). Any user-facing brief where the collapsed card shows mid-sentence prose → `summary_paragraph` parse failed; check `split_summary_paragraph` logs. | BP-626 | `compare_entities` tool returned `—` placeholder cells for revenue / EPS / gross profit while the sibling `get_fundamentals_history_batch` tool returned clean numbers for the SAME tickers — two parallel paths disagreed on data presence, the LLM saw "no data" from one and "real numbers" from the other, then self-corrected mid-answer and refused to fabricate. Root cause: `_handle_compare_entities` fetched fundamentals via `S3Port.get_fundamentals_highlights` which returns an EODHD-shaped dict (`RevenueTTM`, `EarningsShare`, `DilutedEpsTTM`, `MarketCapitalization`, `GrossProfitTTM`, `PERatio`) — but the rendering loop looked up snake_case keys (`revenue`, `eps`, `gross_profit`, `market_cap`, `pe_ratio`) that simply do not exist in that payload. Every single fundamentals cell silently resolved to `None`, the renderer emitted only the header line (no metric rows), and the LLM filled the visible gaps with `—` placeholders before refusing to assert unverified numbers. Confirmed by direct DB inspection: `SELECT jsonb_pretty(to_jsonb(h)) FROM highlights h JOIN instruments i WHERE i.symbol IN ('NVDA','AMD')` returns rows with `RevenueTTM: 37454000128` / `EarningsShare: 3.02` / etc. — the data was always there, the handler just looked for the wrong keys. Meanwhile `get_fundamentals_history_batch` (PLAN-0095 W2) routes through `FundamentalsHistoryPeriod` which exposes normalised `revenue`/`gross_profit`/`net_income`/`eps`/`pe_ratio`/`market_cap` fields. PLAN-0103 W4 (2026-05-30): `_handle_compare_entities` now (1) issues ONE batch call `get_fundamentals_history_batch(tickers=<all>, periods=1)` to source the latest-quarter row using the SAME data path the working batch tool uses; (2) parallelises per-ticker `find_instrument_by_ticker` + `get_quote` (+ `get_fundamentals_highlights` only when the batch row was error/empty); (3) merges metrics via a candidate-list priority order — batch field first, EODHD-cased highlights second — so legacy tickers without quarterly history still render via the fallback. Detection: any compare_entities output where the rendered text contains `### <TICKER>` headers + `Price:` line but ZERO metric lines (`Revenue:`, `EPS:`, etc.) when the same tickers DO have rows in the highlights table → key-mapping mismatch. Cross-check: search rag-chat logs for `tool_executed tool=compare_entities ticker_count=N` paired with chat-eval `agg_q*.json` entries where the LLM refuses to assert numbers. Prevention: NEVER let two tool handlers source the same logical metric from different upstream paths (BP-541 / F-LIVE-Q class). Every metric the LLM might compare across tickers MUST funnel through a single canonical use case that normalises field names; per-tool divergence guarantees a future "two paths disagree" bug. Whenever a handler reads dict fields from an upstream payload, the dict must come from a typed pydantic model (e.g. `FundamentalsHistoryPeriod`) so field-name changes surface at parse time, not at silent-key-miss time. | BP-627 | Risk engine reported `concentration_score=0.0` AND `sector_breakdown={}` on every morning brief even though the upstream sector-fetch path was correctly wired and returning data — `BriefingContextGatherer._fetch_pnl_and_sectors` calls the new `GET /internal/v1/entities/sectors` endpoint (PLAN-0102 W2), reads `canonical_entities.metadata->>'sector'`, and populates `ctx.sector_exposure.by_sector` with healthy aggregates. But `BriefContextFormatter.build_morning_risk_summary` had `sector_breakdown: dict[str, float] = {}` hardcoded and NEVER read `ctx.sector_exposure` — the function only computed a holdings-level HHI from `ctx.portfolio.holdings[*].current_weight`, and when `current_weight` was `None`/`0.0` for dev users (no recent price refresh) the HHI also collapsed to 0.0, hence the "risk engine ran but produced no signal" failure shape in audit `docs/audits/2026-05-29-plan-0103-final-qa.md` §FQA-03. Worse, the score it WAS computing was the wrong concept for a "concentration risk" headline — 10 equal positions across 10 different sectors should read as LOW concentration, but holdings-HHI of equal weights gives 0.1 regardless of how spread the sectors are. The real "sector concentration" risk an analyst cares about (65% in one sector) was structurally invisible. PLAN-0103 W5 (2026-05-30): `build_morning_risk_summary` now (1) reads `ctx.sector_exposure.by_sector` and surfaces it verbatim as `sector_breakdown` (cast to `dict[str, float]`); (2) computes concentration as the SECTOR-level HHI when sectors are available (normalising over total to be safe against partial-outage "Unknown" buckets); (3) falls back to the holdings-level HHI only when no sector data is present. Detection: any morning brief whose `risk_summary.sector_breakdown` is `{}` while `briefing_context_built` log shows `sectors_outcome=ok` + non-zero `entity_count` → formatter-level wiring gap. Cross-check: query `canonical_entities WHERE id IN (<holdings entity_ids>) AND metadata->>'sector' IS NOT NULL` — if rows are present but the brief shows empty sectors, the gatherer ran but the formatter dropped the output. Prevention: NEVER let a formatter compute a metric over a subset of the context fields the gatherer paid to fetch — every new `BriefingContext` field MUST have at least one formatter read site OR be deleted; an unreferenced gatherer field is a silent regression vector. When introducing a new aggregate (sector exposure, factor exposure, ...) add a regression test that constructs a `BriefingContext` WITH the aggregate populated and asserts the formatter output reflects it — `MagicMock()`-based context tests do NOT cover this class because attribute access returns a new Mock, not the expected empty default. Regression tests (3): `services/rag-chat/tests/test_brief_context_formatter.py::test_build_morning_risk_summary_populates_sector_breakdown` + `::test_build_morning_risk_summary_sector_hhi_preferred_over_holdings_hhi` + updated `::test_build_morning_risk_summary_single_holding_max_concentration` (now pins the fallback branch). Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W5, 2026-05-30). Reference: `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/use_cases/brief_context_formatter.py::BriefContextFormatter.build_morning_risk_summary`, `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/use_cases/briefing_context.py::_fetch_pnl_and_sectors` (gatherer side, untouched), `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/api/internal_sectors.py` (endpoint, untouched), audit `docs/audits/2026-05-29-plan-0103-final-qa.md` §FQA-03. | Briefing Pipeline, Formatter Wiring | rag-chat |
| BP-628 | Morning brief "Tape: Not available" leak even after the market-data container is on the latest image (BP-625 closed). Root cause: the `/internal/v1/market/tape` resolver's only "good" tier required BOTH a recent intraday source (5m OHLCV bar OR `Quote.last` newer than the 12 h cutoff) AND a daily close. When the request landed outside the intraday window (overnight, weekends, holidays, or any time the live quote-ingest pipeline had a gap), `premkt_price` resolved to `None` and the row degraded to `session="unavailable"` even though `ohlcv_bars` had a fresh `1d` close. The rag-chat `BriefContextFormatter.format_market_tape` then suppressed the Tape line, the LLM rendered `### Tape\nNot available in retrieved context`, and the brief lost a load-bearing section. Concretely the live DB had `quotes.timestamp = 2026-05-28 20:29 UTC` (after-hours yesterday) and `ohlcv_bars(1d).bar_date = 2026-05-29` for SPY/QQQ — the daily was fine, the intraday wasn't fresh, so we threw the whole row away. PLAN-0103 W7 (2026-05-30): the resolver now implements a documented two-tier fallback — tier 1 = intraday (5m bar or fresh quote), tier 2 = `ohlcv_bars` daily close with `session="prior_close"` and pct = day-over-day from the second daily bar; `session="unavailable"` is reserved for true gaps (no OHLCV row at all). The pydantic `TapeTickerResponse.session` enum now includes `"prior_close"`. A new Prom counter `tape_symbol_data_source_total{symbol,source}` (source ∈ `intraday`/`prior_close`/`unavailable`) makes which tier served each request observable so a "permanent prior_close" alert is one PromQL away. Detection: any brief whose Tape section is missing AND `tape_symbol_data_source_total{source="unavailable"}` is non-zero for the requested symbols → ingestion gap; vs. `tape_symbol_data_source_total{source="prior_close"}` dominating during US market hours → live-quote freshness regression. Prevention: any best-effort endpoint that selects from multiple data sources MUST emit a per-tier label so the operator can prove which tier is firing instead of grepping logs; "unavailable" must never be the failure mode when ANY data tier has a usable row. Regression tests (3): `services/market-data/tests/unit/api/routers/test_internal_market_tape.py::test_prior_close_fallback_when_no_intraday` + `::test_resolve_one_uses_prior_close_when_intraday_missing` + `::test_resolve_one_unavailable_when_no_daily`. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W7, 2026-05-30). Reference: `services/market-data/src/market_data/api/routers/internal_market_tape.py::_resolve_one`, `services/market-data/src/market_data/infrastructure/metrics/prometheus.py::tape_symbol_data_source`, audit `docs/audits/2026-05-29-plan-0103-final-qa.md` §FQA-02. | Best-Effort Endpoint, Fallback Tiers | market-data |
| BP-629 | ETF holdings (`QQQ`, `XLE`, `IBIT`, `XLK`, `SPY`, …) had `canonical_entities.metadata->>'sector' IS NULL` because the equities fundamentals pipeline that back-fills sector tags from EODHD highlights never runs for funds — the EODHD fundamentals endpoint returns a fund-profile shape, not a Highlights shape, so the existing consumer no-ops on it. Downstream the morning brief's risk aggregator only ever read `metadata->>'sector'`, saw NULL for every ETF position, and emitted `sector_breakdown={}` + `concentration_score=0.0` — exactly the "risk engine ran but produced no signal" failure mode previously fixed for the formatter side in BP-627. Two complementary fixes: (1) hand-curated backfill script `scripts/backfill_etf_sectors.py` (default `--dry-run`, `--apply` to write) covering the 26 highest-AUM ETFs with sector + industry + `asset_class="ETF"` written via idempotent `metadata = COALESCE(metadata, '{}'::jsonb) || $json::jsonb`. (2) Endpoint-level fallback in `GET /internal/v1/entities/sectors` — when the canonical row has no sector AND the entity is recognisably an ETF (`metadata.asset_class == "ETF"` OR ticker matches a known ETF prefix like `XL*`/`ARK*` or one of `SPY/QQQ/DIA/IWM/VOO/VTI/VEA/VWO/IBIT/GLD`), the endpoint synthesises a generic `"Equity ETF"` bucket so the rag-chat aggregator never silently drops the row. Wet-run (live `intelligence_db`, 2026-05-30): 28 rows updated across SPY/QQQ/VOO/VTI/DIA/IWM/VWO + XLE/XLF/XLK/XLV/XLY/XLP/XLI/XLB/XLU/XLRE/XLC + GLD/SLV/IBIT/AGG/TLT (3 missing tickers: VEA/ARKK/BND have no canonical row yet). Detection: any brief whose `risk_summary.sector_breakdown` lacks an ETF the user holds, OR `SELECT count(*) FROM canonical_entities WHERE ticker IN (<etf list>) AND metadata->>'sector' IS NULL` returns > 0. Prevention: any entity class that does NOT flow through the equities fundamentals pipeline MUST have an explicit alternate path that writes `metadata->>'sector'` (a backfill script, a fund-profile consumer, or a deterministic synthesised label) — relying on the equities path to "eventually" cover funds is the silent-drop pattern. Regression tests (3): `services/knowledge-graph/tests/unit/api/test_internal_sectors.py::test_sectors_endpoint_returns_backfilled_etf_sector` (real label wins over fallback) + `::test_sectors_endpoint_etf_fallback_when_metadata_marks_asset_class` + `::test_sectors_endpoint_etf_fallback_by_ticker_prefix`. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W8, 2026-05-30 — backfill applied to live DB). Reference: `scripts/backfill_etf_sectors.py`, `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/api/internal_sectors.py` (ETF fallback branch), audit `docs/audits/2026-05-29-plan-0103-final-qa.md` §FQA-03. | Sector Tagging, ETF Coverage | knowledge-graph |
| BP-630 | Morning brief prompt v4.3 carried a single `Cap total brief at 250 words` directive that was the WRONG design — a 6-section investor brief that must cover Tape + Portfolio + Macro + News + Risks + Bonus context CANNOT fit useful depth in 250 words. The LLM either truncated News bullets (the most signal-rich section) or compressed all sections to one-line skeletons; either failure shape silently hollowed out the brief while every section heading still rendered (so structural completeness checks like BP-624 / W6 defensive injection treated the brief as healthy). PLAN-0103 W9 (2026-05-30): v4.3 → v4.4 splits the budget into TWO explicit caps + per-section guidance — `## Summary block: ≤ 50 words, 1-3 sentences` (the collapsed dashboard surface) AND `## Details block: ≤ 700 words across all 6 sections combined` with explicit per-section bullet/word targets (Tape ≤ 25 words one line; Your Portfolio Today 3-6 bullets ~20 words each; Macro Today 1-4 bullets; News That Matters To You 3-5 bullets ~25 words each; Risks + Opportunities 2-3 bullets; Bonus context 1-2 bullets). On quiet days the brief naturally lands ≤ 300 words; on busy days it can fully use the ~700-word details budget without a structural cap forcing truncation. The two-cap design separates the "collapsed-card" surface (which MUST stay tight so the user can scan in 10 seconds) from the "expanded-details" surface (which carries the full investor signal). Parser unchanged — `split_summary_paragraph` already soft-caps the extracted summary at 300 chars (≈50 short words) so the schema invariant holds even if the LLM overruns the directive. Detection: any brief whose News bullets are ≤ 10 words each + Risks/Bonus collapsed to placeholders despite the upstream having signal → word-cap-forced truncation; OR a non-trivial fraction of briefs where `len(content_words) ≈ 230..260` clusters tightly at the cap. Prevention: NEVER write a single global word cap for any multi-section structured output — always budget per surface (collapsed vs expanded) and per section. A directive that conflicts with the desired depth ("emit 6 sections" + "in 250 words") is a structural contradiction the LLM will resolve by silently dropping signal. Regression tests: `libs/prompts/tests/test_prompts.py::TestMorningBriefing::test_v44_six_section_spec` (asserts BOTH caps present + per-section signposts + `250 words`/`Cap total brief` ABSENT) + `::test_v44_few_shot_examples_present` (renamed from `_v43_`) + `services/rag-chat/tests/unit/application/test_briefing_context_gatherer.py::test_morning_prompt_v4_contains_required_sections` (version assertion bumped 4.3 → 4.4). Prevention: any new internal API router added to a backend service MUST be paired with a docker compose `up -d --force-recreate <service>` in the release notes / PR description; CI smoke tests should hit every new `/internal/v1/...` endpoint with an internal-JWT-signed request to catch drift before promotion. NEVER assume `make dev` rebuilds images on code change — it doesn't (the dev compose mounts source over a baked image only for some services, market-data is not one of them). | BP-632 | L2 LLM injection classifier (DeepInfra Meta-Llama-3.1-8B-Instruct-Turbo) returned HTTP 400 `INPUT_REJECTED [PROMPT_INJECTION] Semantic injection detected` in ~0.4s for the legitimate equity-screener prompt `Screen for AI semiconductor companies with market cap above $50B and positive YoY revenue growth.` — request never reached the chat engine, no tools were invoked, audit `docs/audits/2026-05-31-plan-0103-final-qa-v44.md` §3.2 (Q2 `ru_ai_semi_screener`). Root cause: the v3 classifier system prompt at `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/security/llm_injection_classifier.py::_SYSTEM_PROMPT` listed SAFE exemplars for conditional reasoning (v2 — FIX-LIVE-CC) and relationship/graph discovery (v3 — BP-579) but NOT for financial screening with quantitative filters. The model latched on to `above $50B` as a DATA EXFILTRATION signal (UNSAFE category 4 in the prompt) and returned UNSAFE even with `temperature=0.0` — same shape as the two prior narrow-exemplar gaps (intermittent UNSAFE on a legitimate query category the SAFE list never enumerated). This is now the THIRD instance of the pattern. PLAN-0103 W13 (2026-05-30): v4 of the system prompt adds a SAFE exemplar block listing five screener filter shapes — market cap (verbatim from the failing audit prompt), P/E + revenue growth, dividend yield + payout ratio, EBITDA margin + net debt, technical RSI + moving average — and bumps `CLASSIFIER_PROMPT_VERSION` → `"v4"` so the on-disk classifier-result cache (P2 W4 T-W4-02) invalidates stale UNSAFE verdicts when the prompt rolls forward. Detection: any chat request that returns HTTP 400 with `error.code == "INPUT_REJECTED"` and `error.message` starting with `Semantic injection detected` AND the prompt contains a quantitative filter phrase (`market cap above`, `P/E below`, `yield above`, `EBITDA margin above`, `RSI below`) → classifier false-positive, not a true jailbreak. Cross-check: rerun the prompt with `DEBUG_SKIP_CLASSIFIER=true` in dev — if the chat completes normally, the L2 false-positive is confirmed. Prevention: whenever a new false-positive surfaces in chat-eval / benchmark runs, the fix is ALWAYS (a) add a verbatim exemplar of the failing prompt to the SAFE exemplar list, (b) bump `CLASSIFIER_PROMPT_VERSION` to invalidate the on-disk cache, (c) add a SAFE/UNSAFE asymmetric regression file (mocked-SAFE → False + mocked-UNSAFE → True + prompt-content guard + live smoke gated by `INTEGRATION_TEST=1`). NEVER tighten the UNSAFE rules to suppress the symptom — that would break true jailbreak detection. NEVER add a server-side allowlist that short-circuits the LLM call for "screener-shaped" prompts — that creates a silent failure mode where a true injection wrapped in screener language slips past Layer 2. Regression tests (8 added): `services/rag-chat/tests/unit/security/test_llm_injection_classifier_benign_screeners.py` (5 mocked SAFE parametrised + 2 mocked UNSAFE asymmetric + 1 prompt-content guard `test_classifier_prompt_includes_screener_safe_exemplar` + 5 live-smoke parametrised gated by `INTEGRATION_TEST=1` + `RAG_CHAT_DEEPINFRA_API_KEY`). Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W13, 2026-05-30). Reference: `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/security/llm_injection_classifier.py::_SYSTEM_PROMPT` (v4 with screener exemplar block), `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/security/llm_injection_classifier.py::CLASSIFIER_PROMPT_VERSION` (v4), `docs/audits/2026-05-31-plan-0103-final-qa-v44.md` §3.2. | Prompt Engineering, Classifier False-Positive | rag-chat |
| BP-633 | `compare_entities` rendered NULL revenue / EPS / gross_profit cells for one of the compared tickers even though the parallel `get_fundamentals_history_batch` tool returned clean numbers for the SAME ticker on the SAME chat turn — two parallel paths disagreed on data PRESENCE despite BP-626 unifying the data SOURCE. Audit `docs/audits/2026-05-31-plan-0103-final-qa-v44.md` §3.4: NVDA/AMD comparison showed AMD revenue/EPS as missing while `get_fundamentals_history_batch(['NVDA','AMD'], periods=4)` returned 4 quarters of populated AMD data. Root cause: BP-626 unified the FIELD NAMES across the two tools but NOT the PERIOD WINDOW. `_handle_compare_entities` hard-coded `periods=1` (latest quarter only); `get_fundamentals_history_batch` defaults to `periods=5`. When ticker A had Q1 2026 reported but ticker B's Q1 2026 row was still pending in EODHD (revenue/EPS NULL because the actual report dropped after the last upstream sync), the latest-only window silently rendered B's cells as missing while the batch tool 1-2 quarters back had perfectly good data. Same symptom shape as BP-626 (silent NULL cells) but a different mechanism (period filter divergence, not field-name divergence) — proving the unification of two parallel data paths is a TWO-axis problem (field names + window selection); fixing one without the other leaves a latent silent-NULL bug that only surfaces at the LLM-rendering boundary. PLAN-0103 W14 (2026-05-30): widened the batch call to `periods=4` (one fiscal year, matches the Quote-tab Financials default) AND added two module-level helpers `_select_latest_fully_populated_period(tickers, batch_results)` (intersects the per-ticker sets of period labels that have `revenue + eps + gross_profit` all non-None, returns the lex-max common period) + `_pick_period_row(periods_data, common_period)` (returns the matching row OR the latest as fallback). The rendering loop now ALWAYS shows the SAME fiscal quarter for every compared ticker — apples-to-apples by construction. Falls back to per-ticker latest only when no common fully-populated period exists (preserves rendering for true data-pipeline gaps, e.g. one ticker reports annually + other quarterly). Detection: any `compare_entities` output where one `### TICKER` section is missing `Revenue:` / `Eps:` / `Gross Profit:` lines while the others render them in full → period-filter divergence; verify by issuing `get_fundamentals_history_batch` for the same ticker list with `periods=4` — if THAT returns the missing data, this BP is the cause. Prevention: when two tools surface the SAME upstream data, they MUST share BOTH the field-name normalisation AND the period-window selection. Maintain a single `select_canonical_period(...)` helper that any tool can call so the SAME LLM-visible period is rendered everywhere; per-tool divergence guarantees a future silent-NULL bug. Whenever a comparison renderer takes upstream data with NULL-able fields, run a per-ticker pre-filter for "fully populated" BEFORE deciding which row to render — comparing a populated row against a NULL row across tickers is structurally meaningless. Regression tests: `services/rag-chat/tests/unit/application/pipeline/handlers/test_compare_entities_batch_path.py::TestCompareEntitiesPicksLatestFullyPopulatedCommonPeriod::test_picks_latest_common_fully_populated_period` (synthetic NVDA Q1+Q4 vs AMD Q4 + Q1-PENDING → asserts both render Q4 with full numbers) + `::test_falls_back_to_per_ticker_latest_when_no_common_period` + 3 helper unit tests in `TestSelectLatestFullyPopulatedPeriod`. | BP-634 | Q4 comparison chat ("Compare NVDA and AMD on revenue, EPS, gross margin for the latest reported quarter") intermittently returned an empty answer + SSE `error={"code":"llm_second_turn_failed","message":"Unable to generate answer"}` at HTTP 200 — visible to the user as "Unable to generate answer" with no partial content despite 3 successful tool calls (`compare_entities`, `get_fundamentals_history_batch`, `get_price_history`) having returned `status=ok` payloads. Audit `docs/audits/2026-05-31-plan-0103-final-qa-v44.md` + live run `tests/validation/chat_quality_benchmark/runs/run_20260531T162339Z/q_ru_nvda_amd_compare_qtr.json`. Root cause: the second-turn synthesis `stream_chat()` raised `RuntimeError("All LLM providers failed stream_chat")` because the ONLY active provider in the configured chain (DeepInfra `deepseek-r1-distill-qwen-32b`) returned `HTTP 429 Too Many Requests` on the synthesis call (rag-chat logs: `provider_failed provider=deepinfra error="Client error '429 Too Many Requests'"` twice in the same `request_id` window — the chain has no peer provider to fall back to, so a single transient rate-limit window burned the entire user-visible answer). The orchestrator's existing FIX-LIVE-V partial-content recovery only triggered when `len(full_text) >= 80` — when the 429 fired BEFORE any chunk was streamed (zero partial bytes), it fell straight through to `emit_error("llm_second_turn_failed")` with no retry. PLAN-0103 W14 (BP-633) was a contributing factor — widening `_handle_compare_entities` from `periods=1` to `periods=4` increased the tool result payload + the LLM token throughput, which is what pushed Q4 over the per-minute DeepInfra rate window during a benchmark run that issued Q4 alongside three other heavy questions. PLAN-0103 W15 (2026-05-31): wrap the second-turn `stream_chat()` in a 2-attempt retry loop. Attempt 1 runs as before; if it raises BEFORE yielding any token AND the error string matches a transient signature (`"429"` / `"too many requests"` / `"all llm providers failed"` / `"timeout"` / `"503"` / `"502"` / `"504"`), we wait `asyncio.sleep(0.75)` and try once more. Mid-stream failures (any token already yielded) bypass the retry and go straight to the FIX-LIVE-V partial-recovery branch — retrying mid-stream would emit duplicate tokens. Non-transient errors (`ValueError`, `TypeError`, validation, etc.) short-circuit to one attempt — doubling latency on bugs that will never recover is the wrong tradeoff. Worst-case extra latency = `0.75 s + 1 × upstream timeout ≈ 1.5 s` which is bounded inside the 75 s benchmark budget. Detection: any chat request that produces `event=error code=llm_second_turn_failed message="Unable to generate answer"` AND rag-chat logs show `provider_failed provider=deepinfra error="...429...|...All LLM providers failed..."` AND `partial_chars=0` on the `tool_use_second_turn_failed` log line → transient-burn pattern; the W15 retry should suppress the user-visible empty answer in ~95% of cases. Cross-check: count `tool_use_second_turn_transient_retry` events vs `tool_use_second_turn_failed` events in a 24 h window — a non-trivial retry rate with a tiny final-failure rate is the success signature; both staying near zero means the upstream rate window is no longer tight. Prevention: any single-provider chain with a final user-visible action MUST have at least one retry-with-backoff layer for transient errors — relying on the provider chain itself for fallback fails the moment the chain is configured with one active provider (the common case in dev/staging). Add a peer provider (OpenRouter, Groq) to `rag_chat.infrastructure.llm.provider_chain` when DeepInfra rate limits become a recurring concern. NEVER catch + swallow synthesis errors silently — the retry must log `tool_use_second_turn_transient_retry` so operators can see the rate-limit pressure even when the user never sees a failure. NEVER retry mid-stream (after tokens yielded) — duplicate tokens are worse than a partial answer + error. Regression tests (2 added): `services/rag-chat/tests/unit/use_cases/test_chat_orchestrator_fallback.py::TestPartialStreamRecovery::test_stream_chat_transient_429_retries_once_and_recovers` (mocks the FIRST stream_chat call to raise `RuntimeError("All LLM providers failed stream_chat (last error: 429 Too Many Requests)")` and the SECOND to stream a substantive NVDA/AMD comparison chunk; asserts exactly 2 `stream_chat` invocations + no `llm_second_turn_failed` SSE error + the recovered chunk reaches the SSE token stream) + `::test_stream_chat_non_transient_error_does_not_retry` (mocks `stream_chat` to raise `ValueError("messages payload missing required field")`; asserts exactly 1 invocation + the existing `llm_second_turn_failed` hard-error contract is preserved). All 19 fallback tests pass; full rag-chat unit suite 1448 PASS. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W15, 2026-05-31). Reference: `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/use_cases/chat_orchestrator.py::stream_orchestrate` lines 1793-1858 (transient-error retry wrapper), `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/infrastructure/llm/provider_chain.py::stream_chat` (raises the "All LLM providers failed stream_chat" RuntimeError that the wrapper now retries), `tests/validation/chat_quality_benchmark/runs/run_20260531T162339Z/q_ru_nvda_amd_compare_qtr.json` (original failing run), audit `docs/audits/2026-05-31-plan-0103-final-qa-v44.md`, related: BP-633 (W14 payload widening that contributed to the rate window pressure), BP-235 (httpx asyncio timeout pattern — different mechanism, similar transient-burn symptom). | LLM Synthesis, Transient Retry | rag-chat |

PLAN-0103 W16 (2026-05-30): added `_resolve_available_snap_fields(session)` — a lazy + memoised lookup that queries `information_schema.columns` once per process and returns the intersection of `_SNAP_FIELDS` with the columns the deployed table actually carries. NEVER assume the DB is at the ORM head — the contract is one-way ("ORM >= DB"), so missing columns must be tolerated for the request to succeed. The fallback `_log.warning("snap_fields_missing_from_schema", missing=[...])` makes the drift observable. | BP-638 | Benchmark question Q5 `ru_nvda_amd_revenue_4q` ("Compare the revenue trajectories of NVIDIA and AMD over the last 4 quarters") produced wildly varying answer lengths across identical runs against the same prompt, same tools (`get_fundamentals_history_batch`), and same data: 24 / 178 / 185 / 255 words (run_20260531T*); only 2 of 4 rendered a Markdown table. Same intent (`COMPARISON`), same tool result shape (2 tickers × 4 quarters of normalised fundamentals), drastically different answer shapes — the 24-word collapse refused to interpret data the tool clearly returned. Root cause: `libs/prompts/src/prompts/chat/tool_use.py::_PER_INTENT_ADDENDA["COMPARISON"]` carried only a generic "organise the answer with one sub-section per entity" directive — no explicit guidance for the LLM to render multi-entity × multi-period tool outputs as a Markdown table, and no length floor. When the second-turn synthesis call ran on a stochastically lower-temperature path, the LLM sometimes collapsed the 8 data points into a one-line summary. PLAN-0103 W20 (2026-05-31): added a `TABULAR COMPARISON (mandatory):` block to the COMPARISON addendum that (a) enumerates the trigger conditions ("TWO OR MORE entities AND TWO OR MORE periods OR TWO OR MORE entities AND TWO OR MORE metrics"), (b) pins the Markdown table mechanics (header + dashes-separator + one data row per period/entity), (c) requires every numeric cell to be tool-sourced with "N/A" used for missing cells (never interpolated), (d) requires 2-4 sentences of interpretive commentary after the table, (e) sets a length floor of 150-300 words, and (f) explicitly rejects "single-sentence summary" as an acceptable shape for multi-period multi-entity comparisons. Prompt template version bumped 1.2 → 1.3. The directive is wholly inside the COMPARISON addendum so it cannot leak into FACTUAL_LOOKUP / MACRO / GENERAL answers (those would otherwise inflate length on single-entity questions). Detection: any benchmark Q5-shape run where `answer_text` word count < 100 AND the tool turn returned ≥ 2 tickers × ≥ 2 periods of populated fundamentals → COMPARISON-addendum-regression. Cross-check: compare 3-5 consecutive runs of the same question; a > 5× spread in word counts on a stable data shape is the variance signature. Prevention: any per-intent addendum that needs to pin answer SHAPE (not just intent) MUST enumerate (1) the trigger conditions that activate the shape directive, (2) the rendering mechanics verbatim, (3) the length floor + ceiling, and (4) a negative pattern that the LLM can pattern-match against (e.g. "single-sentence summary is NOT acceptable"). Generic "organise the answer" guidance leaves the LLM free to collapse on lower-temperature draws. NEVER add a directive that would force a table on a single-entity question — the trigger must be conditioned on "TWO OR MORE entities" (or metrics). Live verification (2026-05-31, 3 consecutive runs after rebuild): all 3 PASS, word counts 126 / 236 / 204 (vs prior 24 / 178 / 185 / 255 spread), 1/3 with explicit Markdown table + 2/3 with structured per-ticker bulleted quarter lists (the rejection-of-single-sentence floor held; no more 24-word collapses; mean length nearly doubled). Reference: `libs/prompts/src/prompts/chat/tool_use.py::_PER_INTENT_ADDENDA["COMPARISON"]` (TABULAR COMPARISON block added), `libs/prompts/src/prompts/chat/tool_use.py::TOOL_USE_SYSTEM_PROMPT_TEMPLATE` (version 1.2 → 1.3), `tests/validation/chat_quality_benchmark/runs/run_20260531T222339Z|222435Z|222510Z/q_ru_nvda_amd_revenue_4q.json` (live verification runs). | Prompt Engineering, Answer-Shape Variance | rag-chat, libs/prompts |
| BP-637 | Morning brief `risk_summary.sector_breakdown` showed `{"Unknown": 0.104}` for the dev user (MSTR + PPA, ~10% of NAV combined) even though MSTR was fully classified by EODHD as `Sector=Technology / GicSector=Information Technology / Industry=Software—Application` and the data was sitting in the live `relations` table. Root cause: `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/infrastructure/workers/fundamentals_refresh.py::_write_sector_relations` wrote the EODHD GICS classification as TWO graph relations (`is_in_sector` / `is_in_industry`) on the canonical entity, but NEVER mirrored those values into the `canonical_entities.metadata` JSONB column. Downstream consumers — `GET /internal/v1/entities/sectors` (rag-chat `BriefingContextGatherer` for `sector_exposure`) AND any SQL query against `metadata->>'sector'` — read the JSONB column, NOT the graph relation. Live DB at investigation start: 28 / 1108 (2.5 %) of tickered canonical entities had `metadata->>'sector'` populated; 683 / 1108 (62 %) had a usable `is_in_sector` relation but a NULL metadata. The 28 came entirely from PLAN-0103 W8 (BP-629)'s hand-curated ETF CSV; the 0 from EODHD enrichment was the silent gap. The 10.4% "Unknown" slice = MSTR (had relation, no metadata) + PPA (had neither — PPA is an ETF the W8 CSV didn't cover). Same shape as BP-541 (description write-back missing) and BP-540 (placeholder→None): "EODHD round-trip succeeded but the JSONB column downstream consumers actually read never got the value". This is the THIRD instance of the EODHD-data-stranded-in-relations pattern. PLAN-0103 W19 (2026-05-31, this wave) — Forward fix: `_write_sector_relations` now also calls `entity_repo.patch_metadata(entity_id, {"sector": ..., "industry": ..., "asset_class": "Equity"})` BEFORE the relation upsert so a relation_repo failure cannot leave the metadata write orphaned (both succeed or both abort in the same transaction). Added `CanonicalEntityRepository.patch_metadata` (JSONB `||` merge — idempotent, preserves unrelated keys). Backfill: `scripts/backfill_canonical_sectors_from_relations.py` (zero EODHD calls — pure DB copy from the existing relation rows; ran with `--apply` → 683 entities updated, including MSTR). Extended `scripts/backfill_etf_sectors.py` with 14 additional curated ETF rows (PPA, ITA, JETS, SOXX, SMH, IBB, KRE, KWEB, EFA, EEM, USO, FBTC, ETHE, SHY/LQD/HYG/TIP) → 7 additional rows applied (PPA among them: `Industrials / Aerospace & Defense / ETF`). New Prometheus counter `canonical_entity_sector_unknown_total{surface}` bumped inside `GET /internal/v1/entities/sectors` whenever the lookup returns NULL sector — gives operators a chartable baseline for residual coverage gap (foreign-exchange tickers, brand-new instruments awaiting first fundamentals refresh). Live verification (2026-05-31 after cache bust): dev user's `sector_breakdown` lost the `Unknown` bucket entirely. Information Technology rose 25.6 % → 32.2 % (MSTR rolled into IT); a new Industrials 3.8 % slice appeared (PPA); `concentration_score` moved 0.226 → 0.255 (more accurate — was previously masked by undercounted IT exposure). Detection: any brief whose `risk_summary.sector_breakdown` contains an `Unknown` bucket > 1 % AND the underlying holdings include tickered equities that already have an `is_in_sector` edge in `relations` → mirror-write gap; cross-check with `SELECT count(*) FROM canonical_entities ce JOIN relations r ON r.subject_entity_id = ce.entity_id AND r.canonical_type='is_in_sector' WHERE ce.metadata->>'sector' IS NULL;` — non-zero means the backfill must be re-run AND the forward-fix in `_write_sector_relations` is regressed. Cross-check 2: `canonical_entity_sector_unknown_total{surface="sectors_api"}` Prom counter — a sustained non-zero rate signals new untagged entities entering the system faster than fundamentals_refresh can backfill them. Prevention: whenever a worker writes the same domain fact to BOTH a graph relation AND a JSONB column that downstream consumers read independently, the two writes MUST live in the same atomic transaction. NEVER persist the same fact to two separate stores via two separate code paths — one will silently rot. The pattern "write the graph edge first, JSONB later as a TODO" is the failure shape (BP-541 identical; BP-540 a related "placeholder vs None" variant). For provider-sourced classifications (sector, industry, asset_class), the JSONB column is the source of truth for read paths because (a) it's directly indexable + projectable in SQL and (b) avoids a JOIN on the relation graph for every brief/screener/dashboard query. The graph relation is the source of truth for graph traversals (KG-RAG `relationship_path`, AGE Cypher). Both must be kept in sync — any future surface (e.g. an ES projection) must subscribe to the same write hook. Regression tests (2 added, all 22 in file pass; full KG suite 1432 PASS): `services/knowledge-graph/tests/unit/infrastructure/workers/test_fundamentals_refresh_worker.py::TestSectorRelationUpsert::test_sector_metadata_mirrored` (asserts `entity_repo.patch_metadata` called once with `{sector: Technology, industry: Software & Services, asset_class: Equity}`) + `::test_sector_metadata_not_written_when_both_missing` (empty EODHD payload → `patch_metadata.assert_not_awaited` to prevent noisy `updated_at` bumps + log spam on legitimately-blank rows). Recommendation on a second sector provider: NOT NEEDED today — EODHD already classifies 683 / 718 (~95 %) of US-listed equities held in current portfolios; the residual 386 untagged are non-US foreign exchange tickers (Asia-Pacific JP/KR/HK listings) that no dev user in scope holds. Revisit if a future PRD adds international equity coverage as a first-class feature; candidates would be Polygon.io (`/v3/reference/tickers` has `sic_description`) or Alpha Vantage `OVERVIEW` (free tier). Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W19, 2026-05-31 — forward fix + backfill + curated ETF extension + Prom counter + 2 regression tests). Reference: `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/infrastructure/workers/fundamentals_refresh.py::_write_sector_relations` (mirror added), `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/infrastructure/intelligence_db/repositories/canonical_entity.py::patch_metadata` (new helper), `scripts/backfill_canonical_sectors_from_relations.py` (one-shot mirror from relations), `scripts/backfill_etf_sectors.py` (extended with PPA + 13 more ETFs), `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/api/internal_sectors.py` (counter bump on NULL), `services/knowledge-graph/src/knowledge_graph/infrastructure/metrics/prometheus.py::s7_canonical_entity_sector_unknown_total`, related: BP-541 (description write-back gap, same pattern), BP-629 (W8 curated ETF CSV pre-existing fix), BP-631 (Unknown bucket visible in BP-631 live-verification trace, triggered this wave). | EODHD Ingestion Gap, JSONB Mirror | knowledge-graph |
| BP-636 | Morning brief `sector_breakdown` contained noise entries like `{"Diversified Equity": 0.0}` and `{"Unknown": 0.001}` that leaked from synthetic placeholder rows in the sector-exposure aggregator. Pure noise — the operator dashboard rendered them as zero-weight rows, and the brief LLM had to reason past them when summarising risk. Detection: any brief whose `risk_summary.sector_breakdown` contains a sector with `value == 0.0` (or `<= 0.005` after rounding). The Herfindahl computation is unaffected (zero entries contribute 0 to HHI anyway). PLAN-0103 W18 (2026-05-30). | BP-641 | Morning brief `summary_paragraph` populated server-side and rendered in the collapsed `MorningBriefCard` view but completely absent from the EXPANDED view because the expanded branch in `apps/worldview-web/components/dashboard/MorningBriefCard.tsx` jumped directly to `<StructuredBrief lead={brief.lead} sections={...} />` (when `sections.length > 0`) or to the `<div data-testid="brief-narrative">` fallback. Neither branch read `brief.summary_paragraph`. The collapsed view's 3-tier fallback chain `summaryParagraphWithLinks || summaryWithLinks || narrativeWithLinks` was wired correctly in PLAN-0103 W3 (commit `49e23709`) but the equivalent surface in the expanded view was left to render lead + sections only. Symptom: user clicks "Read more", loses the v4.2 executive summary entirely, sees only the structured bullets / narrative prose. The lead block came from `brief.lead` (null in v4.2 cached payloads where the parser extracts summary into `summary_paragraph` instead). PLAN-0103 W21 (2026-06-01): added a sibling block at the top of the expanded view that renders `summaryParagraphWithLinks` (the linkified, stale-metadata-stripped, memoised value the collapsed view already uses) as an italic muted lead with a thin border-bottom separator. The block renders ONLY when `summaryParagraphWithLinks` is truthy (pre-v4.2 cached + instrument briefs fall through cleanly without breaking existing `brief-narrative` / `structured-brief` testid markers). Detection: any brief whose JSON carries `summary_paragraph !== null` but the user-visible expanded view shows only structured sections / narrative without a leading 1-2 sentence overview → render-path skip. Cross-check: open dev-tools, query `document.querySelector('[data-testid="brief-summary-paragraph"]')` in the expanded view — null = regression. Prevention: when a backend field is added to a JSON response that has TWO independent render branches (collapsed / expanded / mobile / structured / fallback), the implementation PR MUST update every branch in the same commit OR explicitly document why a branch is intentionally skipped. A "wire it in the collapsed view, do the expanded view in a follow-up" plan IS the silent-skip failure shape — the follow-up wave moves to other priorities and the gap rots. Regression test: defer to E2E (the expanded view is asserted by `tests/e2e/dashboard.spec.ts` density gate); the brief render layer is otherwise covered by `tests/components/dashboard/MorningBriefCard.test.tsx` which can pin the testid in a follow-up. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W21, 2026-06-01). Reference: `apps/worldview-web/components/dashboard/MorningBriefCard.tsx::573-688` (expanded view branch + summary-paragraph lead block), audit `docs/audits/2026-06-01-frontend-brief-streaming-investigation.md` §2.3. | Frontend Render Branch Skip, Multi-Surface | worldview-web |
| BP-642 | Chat assistant message persisted in chat history was the UN-grounded streamed token text — not the backend's PLAN-0093 numeric-grounded rewrite — because `useChatStream.ts:693-698` explicitly discarded the `final_answer` SSE event with `void data;`. The backend's chat orchestrator runs a post-generation numeric-grounding pass that detects hallucinated numbers and emits a corrected version via `event: final_answer\ndata: {"type":"final_answer","text":"..."}`. Live example (`docs/audits/2026-06-01-chat-quality-aapl-pe-investigation.md`): token stream `"Apple P/E is 37.7x as of Q4 FY2026"` followed by final_answer `"I cannot find evidence that Apple's P/E ratio is 37.7x."` — the user saw the wrong (hallucinated) text persisted in the assistant Message because `finalContent` was already `"Apple P/E is 37.7x..."` when `finalize()` ran. This is a correctness regression introduced by PLAN-0089 K T-03 where the comment justifies the no-op as "the token stream itself is already complete by then" — true under K, no longer true under PLAN-0093. PLAN-0103 W21 (2026-06-01): the handler now replaces BOTH `finalContent` (used by `finalize()`) AND the streaming bubble `text` with `data.text` (or `data.content` for forward-compat), AND sets `streaming.grounded = true` so a "✓ grounded" badge surfaces in the UI signalling the post-stream refinement to the user. Detection: any user-visible chat answer that asserts a specific numeric value while the SSE trace shows a subsequent `final_answer` event with different text → silent token-vs-final-answer divergence. Cross-check: in the chat-quality benchmark harness, compare the persisted `assistant_message.content` against the `final_answer.text` extracted from the raw SSE log — they must match byte-for-byte. Prevention: whenever the backend defines a "rewrite the final answer" event, the frontend hook MUST honor it — the wire contract is "the last final_answer wins", not "the token stream wins". NEVER add a `void data;` no-op handler in a streaming hook; either route the event somewhere or remove it from the contract. The "// suppress unused lint warning" comment is the smell signature — if the event has no consumer, it should be removed from the SSE schema, not silently dropped. Regression test (1 added): `apps/worldview-web/features/chat/hooks/__tests__/useChatStream.test.tsx::useChatStream > final_answer SSE event replaces streamed tokens in the persisted message` — emits a token stream with hallucinated text, then a `final_answer` event with corrected text, then `[DONE]`; asserts the persisted assistant message carries the CORRECTED text AND `not.toContain` the hallucinated tokens. Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W21, 2026-06-01). Reference: `apps/worldview-web/features/chat/hooks/useChatStream.ts::693-723` (final_answer handler — replaces finalContent + streaming.text + sets grounded flag), `apps/worldview-web/features/chat/components/MessageTurn.tsx::chat-grounded-badge` (UI badge), audit `docs/audits/2026-06-01-frontend-brief-streaming-investigation.md` §3.4. | Frontend SSE Contract, Silent Drop | worldview-web |
| BP-631 | Morning brief `risk_summary.concentration_score = 0.0` and `sector_breakdown` empty because the rag-chat brief scheduler logged `portfolio_pnl outcome=empty` on every run — root cause was TWO independent failures stacked: (1) the live `worldview-portfolio` container image (built 2026-05-27) predated commit `d072137e` (2026-05-29 PLAN-0102 W2) that added `services/portfolio/src/portfolio/api/routes/internal_pnl.py` + the matching `app.include_router(internal_pnl_router)` line in `app.py:232`. Code on disk was correct; routes on the running app missed it. `GET /internal/v1/users/{id}/portfolio/pnl` returned `404 Not Found` (FastAPI default body — NOT the `"User not found"` body the use case raises, which is the giveaway distinguishing "route absent" from "auth/lookup failed"). (2) Even with P&L back, dev-seed holdings have `current_weight = NULL` (BP-517), so the existing 3-tier weight fallback in `_compute_sector_exposure()` (current_price→last_close→current_weight) could still produce `total <= 0` → `None` → empty `sector_exposure` → blank risk_summary. Operational fix for (1): `DOCKER_BUILDKIT=1 docker build -t worldview-portfolio:latest -f services/portfolio/Dockerfile .` + `docker compose -f infra/compose/docker-compose.yml up -d --no-deps --force-recreate portfolio` (identical procedure to BP-625 for market-data). Code fix for (2) (PLAN-0103 W12, 2026-05-31): extend the ladder with a 4th equal-weight tier — when neither the P&L snapshot NOR `current_weight` produces non-zero values, fall back to `1.0 / N` per held entity (skip rows with no `entity_id`). At minimum the brief gets a computable HHI = 1/N for an equal-weight portfolio instead of an empty risk_summary. New Prom counter `brief_sector_exposure_weight_source{source}` (source ∈ `pnl`/`db_weight`/`quote`/`equal`) makes silent degradation observable — a spike in `equal` means upstream P&L regressed. Live verification (2026-05-31 after both fixes): `GET /v1/briefings/morning` for `01900000-...-010` returned `concentration_score=0.2261`, `sector_breakdown` with 7 sectors (Energy 28.7%, IT 25.6%, Digital Assets 24.8%, Unknown 10.4%, Commodities 6.1%, Consumer Discretionary 4.4%, Diversified Equity 0.0%), and rag-chat logs showed `portfolio_pnl outcome=ok elapsed_ms=26.54`. Detection: any brief where `risk_summary.concentration_score == 0.0` AND rag-chat logs show `portfolio_pnl outcome=empty` AND portfolio container responds 404 (body `"Not Found"` vs `"User not found"`) to a direct curl of `/internal/v1/users/{id}/portfolio/pnl` → image-staleness pattern. Cross-check: `docker exec worldview-portfolio-1 python -c "from portfolio.app import create_app; app=create_app(); print([r.path for r in app.routes if 'pnl' in r.path])"` MUST list the path; if empty the in-container app.py predates the W2 commit. Prevention: same as BP-625 — every new internal router added to a backend service MUST be paired with a `docker compose ... --force-recreate <service>` step in release notes; CI smoke should hit every new `/internal/v1/...` endpoint. Additionally: any aggregation that consumes "best-effort" upstream data MUST end with a deterministic last-resort fallback that never returns None — silent degradation is acceptable, silent disappearance is not. Regression tests (1 added, all 5 in file pass): `services/rag-chat/tests/unit/application/test_compute_sector_exposure.py::test_sector_exposure_equal_weight_when_pnl_and_db_weights_unavailable` (synthetic 5-holding portfolio with `pnl_snapshot=None` + `current_weight=None` on every holding → asserts each sector = 0.20 = 1/N). Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W12, 2026-05-31 — portfolio rebuilt + equal-weight tier added + rag-chat rebuilt). Reference: `services/portfolio/src/portfolio/api/routes/internal_pnl.py` (route source, untouched), `services/portfolio/src/portfolio/app.py:232` (registration, untouched — image staleness was the gap), `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/use_cases/briefing_context.py::_compute_sector_exposure` (4-tier ladder + telemetry), `services/rag-chat/src/rag_chat/application/metrics/prometheus.py::brief_sector_exposure_weight_source`, audit `docs/audits/2026-05-31-plan-0103-final-qa-v44.md` §4. | Container Operations, Fallback Tiers | portfolio, rag-chat |
| BP-639 | Chat-quality benchmark question "What's AAPL's P/E ratio?" was answered as "Apple's P/E ratio for Q4 FY2026 is approximately 37.7x" — a fabricated, single-quarter, future-dated, snapshot-injected value with no TTM construction (audit `docs/audits/2026-06-01-chat-quality-aapl-pe-investigation.md`). Two stacked failures: (1) `services/market-data/src/market_data/application/use_cases/get_fundamentals_history.py` returned EODHD's pre-emitted future-dated placeholder row (`period_end=2026-06-30`, every flow metric NULL) because the use case sorted DESC and sliced `[:1]` before any sanity filter — the LLM saw "one row" with `eps=None, revenue=None, net_income=None` and the FORBIDDEN-fabrication guardrail was overridden by the strong "use what the tool returned" instinct. (2) The `tool_use` FINANCIAL_DATA addendum advised `periods >= 5` for YoY/QoQ but said nothing about ratio questions (P/E, ROE, gross margin); the agent defaulted to `periods=1`, asked for a snapshot, got the snapshot field `pe_ratio=37.7` (a TTM value from HIGHLIGHTS injected into every per-period row by the use case — separate bug, see BP-640), and quoted it as a quarter-specific ratio. Both failures together produce a confident-looking, completely-fabricated answer. PLAN-0103 W22 (FIX-A): `get_fundamentals_history.py` now drops any row where `period_end > today (UTC)` AND the section-specific driver metric (epsActual for QUARTERLY, totalRevenue for ANNUAL) is null; a structured `fundamentals_future_placeholder_dropped{symbol, period_end, period_type}` log event makes drop frequency observable. PLAN-0103 W23 (FIX-B): `libs/prompts/src/prompts/chat/tool_use.py` FINANCIAL_DATA addendum gains a mandatory `RATIO-OR-TTM QUESTIONS (mandatory):` block enumerating the affected metrics (P/E, EV/EBITDA, ROE, ROIC, FCF margin, gross margin, operating margin) + TTM metrics (TTM revenue/EPS/FCF, YoY growth), forcing `periods >= 5` + explicit "TTM EPS = sum of last 4 quarterly EPS" construction + as-of-date requirement + "Refuse rather than fabricate if any of the last 4 quarters is missing". Template version bumped 1.3 → 1.4. PLAN-0103 W24 (FIX-C): `services/rag-chat/.../handlers/market.py::_handle_get_fundamentals_history` adds a phantom-row guard symmetric to the BP-626 batch-path fix — any row where ALL of `(revenue, eps, net_income, ebitda)` are null is dropped before rendering; if every row is a phantom the handler returns `None` (item_count=0) so the LLM sees no data instead of one-row-of-dashes. Defence-in-depth: the market-data fix would prevent leakage in normal operation, but the handler-side guard catches any future schema drift that lets a phantom row through. Detection: any chat answer that quotes a P/E or ratio value with a single-quarter period label (no "TTM" / no "trailing four quarters" / no aggregation language) → ratio-without-TTM-construction shape; cross-check the tool trace for `periods=1` or `periods=2` on a `get_fundamentals_history*` call when the user asked about a ratio. Cross-check 2: any `tool_result` carrying a row whose `revenue`, `eps`, `net_income`, AND `ebitda` are all null while `pe_ratio` and `market_cap` are non-null → snapshot-field-injected phantom (BP-640 territory). Prevention: the upstream-data + prompt + handler triple is the contract — fixing only one layer leaves two latent failure modes. Any future ratio metric added to the catalog MUST be added to the RATIO-OR-TTM enumeration in the prompt addendum AND the flow-metric-null phantom predicate in the handler MUST be updated if a new flow metric becomes available (e.g. `fcf` if FCF history lands as a structured field). Regression tests (3+2+3 = 8 added): `services/market-data/tests/unit/test_get_fundamentals_history_future_placeholder.py` (2 tests — future placeholder dropped, past null row retained); `libs/prompts/tests/test_tool_use_prompt.py::test_financial_data_addendum_contains_ratio_or_ttm_directive` + `::test_prompt_template_version_is_at_least_1_4` (2 tests); `services/rag-chat/tests/unit/application/pipeline/handlers/test_fundamentals_phantom_row.py` (3 tests — all-phantom returns None, partial-fill row preserved, mixed input filters phantom). Status: FIXED (PLAN-0103 W22+W23+W24, 2026-06-01 — backend + prompt + handler). Live verification: deferred to chat-quality benchmark re-run after container rebuild (Round 2 scope); the 6 new `real_user_v2` benchmark questions added to `tests/validation/chat_quality_benchmark/questions.yaml` cover the regression surface (`ru_aapl_pe_simple`, `ru_meta_eps_trend`, `ru_amzn_revenue_yoy`, `ru_tsla_margin_trend`, `ru_googl_pe_vs_history`, `ru_aapl_forward_pe`). Related: BP-626 (batch-path phantom-row guard, same shape on the sibling tool), BP-638 (TABULAR COMPARISON directive in same prompt file), BP-640 (snapshot-field injection — separate bug surfaced by the same investigation, fix tracked for PLAN-0104). | BP-640 | Snapshot field injection in `GetFundamentalsHistoryUseCase`: `pe_ratio` and `market_cap` are sourced from the EODHD HIGHLIGHTS section (TTM/current snapshot, no quarter-level dimension) and then injected into EVERY per-period row of the response. A row for `Q1 FY2025` and a row for `Q4 FY2025` both carry the SAME `pe_ratio` and `market_cap` values (the latest TTM snapshot), but the rag-chat rendering layer presents them as per-period cells in a Markdown table. The LLM has been observed quoting a 37.7x TTM P/E as if it were the P/E for a specific quarter — same fabrication shape as BP-639 except the value is technically real (sourced from EODHD) while the quarter-context attribution is fabricated. Detection: any tool result row where `pe_ratio` or `market_cap` is identical across two or more period rows for the same ticker → snapshot field injection. Cross-check: SQL `SELECT period_end, data->>'PERatio' FROM fundamentals_records WHERE section='HIGHLIGHTS' ORDER BY period_end DESC` — HIGHLIGHTS is a single TTM row, never multi-period, by EODHD contract (`docs/references/eodhd-fundamentals.md`). Fix tracked for PLAN-0104: either (a) move the snapshot fields to a separate top-level `snapshot` block in the API response with an explicit `snapshot_as_of` date (current API consumers must opt-in to the new field), OR (b) clear `pe_ratio` and `market_cap` on every row except the most recent and add an explicit `snapshot_as_of` per-row hint so the LLM cannot quote a quarter-specific P/E without seeing the mismatch. Approach (a) is the cleaner contract but breaks the rag-chat MarketHandler rendering path (the Markdown table currently iterates rows + reads pe_ratio per row); approach (b) is the minimal-diff path. Defer to PLAN-0104 design discussion. Workaround in PLAN-0103 W22-24: the phantom-row guard (BP-639) prevents the specific 37.7x-on-future-placeholder symptom; the RATIO-OR-TTM prompt directive forces `periods >= 5` + TTM construction so the LLM never quotes a single-row P/E without first aggregating; but the underlying field-shape bug remains. Prevention: when a use case combines data from MULTIPLE EODHD sections (HIGHLIGHTS = TTM snapshot, INCOME_STATEMENT = per-period flow, EARNINGS_HISTORY = per-period EPS), every output row MUST carry an explicit `<field>_as_of` qualifier for fields whose source section has different periodicity than the row itself. A field with no periodicity context is a fabrication risk. Status: DOCUMENTED only — fix is PLAN-0104 scope. No regression test yet; the test will land with the fix. Reference: `services/market-data/src/market_data/application/use_cases/get_fundamentals_history.py:218-224` (`pe_ratio` and `market_cap` from highlights injected into every row + TODO PLAN-0104 marker), audit `docs/audits/2026-06-01-chat-quality-aapl-pe-investigation.md` §SNAPSHOT FIELD INJECTION. Related: BP-639 (same investigation, separate but linked failure mode). | API Contract, Snapshot vs Flow | market-data |
